<p class=MsoNormal>1) Identify the following types of isomers, for ten points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They differ in the covalent arrangements of their atoms,
such as butane and isobutane.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>structural</u> isomers</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have the same covalent partnerships, but they differ in
their spatial arrangements, such as cis-but-2-ene and trans-but-2-ene.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>geometric</u> isomers</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They are mirror images of each other, such as L-Dopa and
D-Dopa.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>enantiomers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>2) Answer the following about organic functional groups and
compounds important in biochemistry, for 2 and 4/13 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the functional group consisting of a hydrogen atom
bonded to an oxygen atom, which is bonded to a carbon skeleton, and give the
name of compounds containing this functional group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hydroxyl</u>; <u>alcohol</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the functional group consisting of a carbon atom joined
to an oxygen atom by a double bond, and give the name of compounds containing
this group at the end of their carbon skeleton, and give the name of compounds
containing this group elsewhere in the carbon skeleton.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>carbonyl</u>; <u>aldehyde</u>; <u>ketone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the functional group consisting of an oxygen atom
double-bonded to a carbon atome that is also bonded to a hydroxyl <span
class=GramE>group, and</span> give the name of compounds containing this group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>carboxyl</u>; <u>carboxylic acids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the functional group consisting of a nitrogen atom
bonded to two hydrogen atoms and to the carbon <span class=GramE>skeleton, and</span>
give the name of compounds containing this group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>amino;</u> <u>amines</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the functional group consisting of a sulfur atom bonded
to an atom of <span class=GramE>hydrogen, and</span> give the name of compounds
containing this group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sulfhydryl</u>; <u>thiols</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the functional group consisting of a phosphate ion
covalently attached by one of its oxygen atoms to the carbon <span class=GramE>skeleton,
and</span> give the name of compounds containing this group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phosphate</u>; <u>organic phosphates<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>3) Identify the following terms related to biochemical
bonding from their definitions, for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A reaction in which two molecules are covalently bonded to
each other through the loss of a small molecule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>condensation</u> reaction</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A specific type of condensation reaction in which the
molecule lost is water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>dehydration</u> reaction</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A reaction in which bonds are broken by the addition of
water molecules; it is the reverse of a dehydration reaction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hydrolysis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A long molecule consisting of many identical or similar
building blocks linked by covalent bonds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>polymers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The repeating molecular units which serve as the building
blocks of a polymer.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>monomers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of bonds between monosaccharides in sugars.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glycosidic</u> linkages</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of bonds between amino acids in proteins.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>peptide</u> bonds</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>4) Answer the following about monosaccharides, for 2.5
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Monosaccharides can be divided into two major categories. In
one, the carbonyl group is located on the end of the carbon skeleton, while in
the other it is one away from the end. Name these two categories, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aldoses</u> (aldehyde sugars); <u>ketoses</u> (ketone sugars)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Most monosaccharides can also be categorized based on how
many carbon atoms they contain as triose sugars, pentose sugars, or hexose
sugars. For each of the following monosaccharides, classify it based on both
its carboyl location and its number of carbons. For example, if I said glucose,
you would obviously answer &quot;aldose, hexose&quot;.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Ribose</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aldose, pentose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fructose</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ketose, hexose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Glyceraldehyde</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aldose, triose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Galactose</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aldose, hexose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Ribulose</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ketose, pentose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>5) Given a disaccharide, name its two component
monosaccharides, for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Maltose</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glucose, glucose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Lactose</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glucose, galactose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sucrose</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glucose, fructose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>6) Identify the following polysaccharides from their
descriptions, for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A polymer of glucose monomers found in plants, and normally
connected by 1-4 linkages, it stores energy.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>starch</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The simplest, unbranched form of starch.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>amylose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A branched form of starch with 1-6 linkages at the branch
points.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>amylopectin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A highly branched polymer of glucose which stores energy in
animals, usually in the liver and muscles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glycogen</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The most abundant organic compound on Earth, it is similar
to starch except that the glucose monomers are in the Beta ring formation
rather than the Alpha ring formation, and it is a major component of the cell
walls in plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cellulose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A polysaccharide of glucose molecules with
nitrogen-containing appendages, it is leathery but hardens when encrusted with
calcium <span class=GramE>carbonate, and</span> is used to build exoskeletons
in arthropods.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chitin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>7) Answer the following related to lipids, for three points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fats consist of two major components. The first is an
alcohol with three carbons, each bearing a hydroxyl group. The second is a
chain of usually 16 to 18 carbons, with a carboxyl group at one end. Name these
two components, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glycerol</u>; <u>fatty acid<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fats can be classified into these two categories based on
whether there are any double bonds between carbon atoms in the fatty acid
hydrocarbon tail.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>saturated, unsaturated</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Another term for a fat, this word reflects the fact that a
fat consists of three fatty acids linked to one glycerol molecule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>triacylglycerol</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These lipids are <span class=GramE>similar to</span> fats,
except that one of the fatty acids is replaced by a phosphate group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phospholipids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term describes a molecule which is both hyrdophobic and
hydrophilic, such as phospholipids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ambivalent</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These are circular clusters of phospholipids which form in
water, with the hydrophilic phosphate heads on the outside and the hydrophobic
hydrocarbon tails on the inside.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>micelle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This is a type of lipid characterized by a carbon skeleton
consisting of four fused rings. Many <span class=GramE>function</span> as
hormones.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>steroids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Many other steroids are synthesized from this steroid, which
is a common component of animal cell membranes, but which may contribute to
atherosclerosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cholesterol</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>8) Answer the following about amino acids, for five points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An amino acid consists of a carbon atom bound to a hydrogen
atom, a side chain unique to each amino acid, and two functional groups. Name
the two functional groups.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>amino, carboxyl</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are twenty amino acids found in proteins, each
distinguished by its side chain. Given a description of its side chain,
identify the following amino acids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The simplest amino acid, its side chain is just a hydrogen
atom.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glycine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Its side chain is a methyl group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>alanine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Its side chain is an isopropyl group, and when it
substitutes for glutamic acid in red blood cell proteins, it causes sickle-cell
anemia.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>valine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Its side chain is a sulfhydryl group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cysteine<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>9) Answer the following concerning the four levels of
protein structure, for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A protein's primary structure is its unique sequence of this
type of molecule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>amino acids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A protein's secondary structure is the series of coils and
folds which determine its conformation. One of the two most common types of
secondary structures is a delicate coil held together by hydrogen bonding
between every fourth amino acid, whereas in the other type, two regions of the
polypeptide chain lie parallel to each other, with their backbones hydrogen
bonded to each other. Name these two structures, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>alpha-helix</u>; <u>pleated sheet</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A protein's tertiary structure consists of irregular
contortions from bonding between side chains of the various amino acids. When
two cysteine monomers are brought close together, this type of covalent bond
can form, riveting parts of the protein together.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>disulfide bridge</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A protein may consist of more than one polypeptide chain,
and the combination of these chains is known as the protein's quaternary
structure. When proteins fold, they are sometimes assisted by other proteins,
known by this name, that serve as temporary braces.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chaperone proteins<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>10) Answer the following about nucleotides, for 4 and 2/7
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Nucleotides consist of three major components. Name them.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nitrogenous base, pentose (prompt on sugar), phosphate group</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A nitrogenous base bound to a pentose sugar, without a
phosphate group, is known by this term.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nucleoside</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>DNA differs from RNA in that its component pentose is
lacking an oxygen on its number two carbon. Name the pentoses in DNA and in
RNA, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>deoxyribose</u>, <u>ribose</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>RNA molecules also differ from DNA molecules in that the
nitrogenous base thymine is replaced by this other nitrogenous base.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>uracil</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>11) Nitrogenous bases can be classified into two families. The
first is characterized by six-membered rings of carbon and nitrogen atoms,
while the second is characterized by a six-membered ring fused to a
five-membered ring. Name these two families, respectively, for 4 and 2/7 points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pyrimidines</u>; <u>purines</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three members of the pyrimidine family, for 4 and
2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytosine, thymine, uracil</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three members of the purine family, for 4 and 2/7
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>adenine, guanine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>12) Answer the following concerning the chemical processes
in an organism, for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The totality of an organism's chemical processes is known by
this term, which comes from the Greek for &quot;to change&quot;.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>metabolism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Metabolism can be divided into processes which release
energy by breaking down complex molecules to simpler compounds, and those
processes which consume energy to build complicated molecules from simpler
ones. Name these two processes, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>catabolism</u>; <u>anabolism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are two main types of catabolic pathways. In one,
oxygen is consumed as a reactant along with the organic fuel. In the other,
sugars are partially degraded without the help of oxygen. Name these two
pathways, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cellular respiration</u>; <u>fermentation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>13) Identify the following terms related to biological
catalysts from their definitions, for three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for catalytic proteins.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>enzymes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The reactant on which an enzyme <span class=GramE>acts</span>.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>substrate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The region of an enzyme molecule which <span class=GramE>actually
binds</span> to the substrate, typically a pocket or groove on its surface.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>active site</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Nonprotein molecules which assist enzymes, usually by
binding permanently or reversibly to the active site.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cofactors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Organic molecules which act as cofactors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coenzymes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Molecules which resemble the structure of a substrate and
compete for admission to the active site, reducing the productivity of enzymes
by blocking the substrates from entering the active sites.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>competitive inhibitors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Molecules which bind to some part of an enzyme other than
its active site, causing it to change conformation, making its active site
unreceptive to its substrate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>noncompetitive inhibitors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A receptor site on an enzyme to which noncompetitive
inhibitors can bind.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>allosteric site</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The process by which a metabolic pathway is turned off by
its end-product, which acts as an inhibitor of an enzyme within the pathway.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>feedback inhibition</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An interaction of the constituent subunits of a protein
causing a conformational change in one subunit to be transmitted to all the
others.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cooperativity</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>14) Identify the following instruments used in the study of
cells, for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this type of microscope, visible light is passed through
the specimen and then through glass lenses, which refract the light in such as
way that the image is magnified as it is projected into the eye.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>light</u> microscope</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this type of microscope, a beam of electrons is focused
using electromagnets through sections of preserved cells stained with atoms of
heavy metals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transmission electron microscope</u> (prompt on just electron microscope)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this type of microscope, the electron beam scans the
surface of the sample, which is coated with a thin film of gold, producing a
three-dimensional topography of the specimen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>scanning electron microscope</u> (prompt on jus electron microscope)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These machines, which spin at up to 80,000 rpm, are used for
cell fractionation, separating the major organelles so their individual
functions may be studied.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ultracentrifuge</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>15) Answer the following about the basics of cells, for six
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cells may be classified into two major categories. One,
whose name comes from the Greek for &quot;before kernel&quot;, has no nucleus. The
other, whose name comes from the Greek for &quot;true kernel&quot;, has a
membrane-bound nucleus and membrane-bound organelles. Name these two
categories, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>prokaryotes</u>; <u>eukaryotes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The DNA in a prokaryote is concentrated in a region known by
this name.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nucleoid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The entire region between the nucleus in a eukaryote and the
cell membrane is known by this name.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytoplasm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cytoplasm consists of organelles suspended in this
semifluid medium.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytosol</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>16) In this bonus, and the eight which follow, we will
examine the components of a eukaryotic cell. In this bonus, identify the
following terms related to the nucleus, for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A double membrane, each a lipid bilayer with associated
proteins, which is perforated by pores and surrounds the nucleus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
nuclear <u>envelope<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A netlike array of protein filaments which lines the nuclear
side of the nuclear envelope and maintains the shape of the nucleus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nuclear lamina</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Material within the nucleus consisting of DNA organized
along with proteins.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chromatin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Chromatin that is coiled into thick structures as the cell
prepares to divide.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chromosomes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A structure within the nucleus where components of ribosomes
are synthesized.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nucleolus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>17) Identify the following terms related to the endomembrane
system from their definitions, for 3.75 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An extensive membranous network which is continuous with the
outer nuclear membrane, composed of ribosome-studded and ribosome-free regions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endoplasmic reticulum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The network of membranous tubules and sacs which compose
endoplasmic reticulum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cisternae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The internal compartment of endoplasmic reticulum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cisternal space</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This structure receives transport vesicles with materials
produced by the endoplasmic reticulum at its cis-<span class=GramE>face, and</span>
releases its products from its trans-face.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Golgi apparatus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A membrane-bounded sac of hydrolytic enzymes which the cell
uses to digest macromolecules.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lysosome<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The two types of membrane-bound sacs in the cell,
differentiated by their size.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vesicles, vacuoles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The membrane which encloses the large central vacuole in
mature plant cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tonoplast</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>18) Identify the following terms related to the site of
cellular respiration from their definitions, for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The organelle in which cellular respiration takes place</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mitochondrion</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The infoldings of the mitochondrion's inner membrane, which
give the membrane a large surface area, enhancing the productivity of cellular
respiration.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cristae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The compartment in the mitochondrion within the inner
membrane, in which some of the metabolic steps of cellular respiration take
place.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mitochondrial matrix</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>19) Identify the following terms related to plastids in
plant cells from their definitions, for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Colorless plastids which store starch, particularly in roots
and tubers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>amyloplasts<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Plastids which are rich in pigments which give fruits and
flowers their orange and yellow hues.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chromoplasts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Plastids which contain the green pigment chlorophyll along
with enzymes and other molecules that function in the photosynthetic production
of food.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chloroplasts<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The membranous system of flattened sacs inside the
chloroplast.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thylakoids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>Structures of thylakoids,</span> stacked
like poker chips.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>grana</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The fluid outside the thylakoids inside a chloroplast.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stroma</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>20) Identify the following terms related cell organelles not
included in the previous bonuses, from their definitions, for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The sites where the cell makes proteins; they can be either
free or bound.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ribosomes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Membrane-bound compartments which transfer hydrogen from
substrates to oxygen, used to break down large molecules or detoxify harmful
compounds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>peroxisomes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Peroxisomes produce this toxic chemical as a <span
class=GramE>by-product, but</span> contain enzymes to convert it to water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hydrogen peroxide</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Specialized peroxisomes in the fat-storing tissues of plant
seeds which convert fatty acids to sugar.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glyoxysomes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>21) Identify the following terms relating to the network of
fibers in the cytoplasm of a cell from their definitions, for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for the entire network of fibers in the
cytoplasm which contributes to cell organization and activity.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytoskeleton</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are three major components of the cytoskeleton. Identify
them from their descriptions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These fibers are hollow tubes made of alpha and beta
tubulin, which form compression-resisting girders, contribute to cell motility,
move chromosomes in cell division, and move organelles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>microtubules</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These fibers are two intertwined strands of actin, which function
in cytoplasmic streaming, cell motility, tension-bearing, and cell division.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>microfilaments</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These fibers are proteins of the keratin family supercoiled
into thick cables, which anchor some organelles, form nuclear lamina, and bear
tension.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>intermediate filaments</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the region near the nucleus which is also known as the
microtubule-organizing center, from which microtubules grow.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cerntrosome</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the pair of structures in animal cells which are
composed of nine sets of triplet microtubules arranged in a <span class=GramE>ring,
and</span> replicate during cell division.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>centrioles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>22) Identify the following terms related to cell motility
from their definitions, for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A locomotive appendage which undulates, driving a cell in
the same direction as the axis of the appendage; there are usually no more than
one or a few per cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>flagellum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Locomotive appendages which work like oars, moving the cell
in a direction perpendicular to its axis; there may be many per cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cilia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cellular extensions by which a cell can crawl along a
surface in ameboid movement.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pseudopodia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The two proteins which are interdigitated in muscle cells,
and whose contractions and extensions can cause movement.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>actin, myosin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A large contractile protein which forms the sidearms of
microtubule doublets in cilia and flagella.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>dynein</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A structure <span class=GramE>similar to</span> a centriole
which anchors a cilium or flagellum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>basal body<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>23) There are three main types of interceullular junctions
in animals. Identify them from their descriptions, for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These connections form continuous belts around the cell, and
the membranes of neighboring cells are <span class=GramE>actually fused</span>,
forming a seal that prevents leakage of extracellular fluid.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tight</u> junctions</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These <span class=GramE>junctions</span> function like
rivets, fastening cells together into strong epithelial sheets.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>desmosomes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These connections provide cytoplasmic channels between
adjacent cells, and special membrane proteins surround each pore, which is wide
enough for small molecules to pass through.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gap</u> junctions</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>24) Identify the following terms related to the substance in
which animal tissue cells are embedded from their definitions, for five points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for the substance of proteins and
polysaccharides in which animal tissue cells are embedded.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>extra-cellular matrix</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for proteins covalently bonded to
carbohydrates, which are the major component of the extra-cellular matrix.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glycoproteins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The most abundant protein in animals, it forms strong fibers
in the extra-cellular matrix and is found extensively in connective tissue and
bone.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>collagen</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of glycoprotein containing up to 95% carbohydrate
which forms complex networks in the extra-cellular matrix.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>proteoglycans</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Receptor proteins which are built into the plasma membrane,
spanning the <span class=GramE>membrane</span> and bound to microfilaments of
the cytoskeleton, allowing them to transmit changes in the extra-cellular
matrix to the cytoskeleton and vice versa.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>integrins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of glycoprotein in the extra-cellular matrix which
bind to integrins.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fibronectins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>25) Answer the following related to cell membranes, for 7.5
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The currently accepted model of cellular membranes holds
that proteins are dispersed and individually inserted into a bilayer of
phospholipids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fluid mosaic</u> model</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are two major types of membrane proteins. One type are
generally trans-membrane proteins, with hydrophobic regions that completely
span the hydrophobic interior of the membrane. The other type <span
class=GramE>are</span> not embedded in the lipid bilayer but rather are
appendages loosely to the surface of the membrane. Name these two types,
respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>integral</u> proteins; <u>peripheral</u> proteins</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Most membrane carbohydrates are branched with fewer than 15
sugar units, known by this name, from the Greek for &quot;few&quot;.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oligosaccharides</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>26) Identify the following terms related to passive
transport from their definitions, for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The tendency for molecules of any substance to spread out
into the available space.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>diffusion</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The difference in molecules of a substance per volume in two
different regions, down which the substance will diffuse.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>concentration gradient</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The diffusion of water across a selectively permeable
membrane.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>osmosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The control of water balance in a cell</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>osmoregulation<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give, respectively, the relative terms for a solution with
higher concentration, lower concentration, and the same concentration as a
given solution.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hypertonic</u>; <u>hypotonic</u>; <u>isotonic</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>27) A cell may gain or lose water depending on the
concentration of its environment relative to itself. Give, respectively, the
terms for an animal cell in hypertonic, isotonic, and hypotonic solutions, for
five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>shriveled</u>; <u>normal</u>; <u>lysed</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give, respectively, the terms for a plant cell in
hypertonic, isotonic, and hypotonic solutions, for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>plasmolyzed</u>; <u>flaccid</u>; <u>turgid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>28) Answer the following related to active transport, for
7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>One of the most important transport systems in cells is a
pump which creates steep concentration gradients by transporting three
molecules of one cation out of the cell for every two molecules of another
cation pumped into the cell. Name the two cations, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sodium</u>; <u>potassium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This type of pump actively transports hydrogen ions out of
the cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>proton pump</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Transports, such as the sodium-potassium pump and the proton
pump, which generate a voltage across a membrane by transferring charge across
the membrane, are known by this name.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>electrogenic pump</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>29) Identify the following terms related to the transport of
large molecules across a membrane from their definitions, for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The secretion of macromolecules out of the cell by the
fusion of vesicles with the plasma membrane.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>exocytosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The reception of macromolecules and particulate matter into
the cell by forming new vesicles from the plasma membrane.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endocytosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of endocytosis in which a cell engulfs a particle by
wrapping pseudopodia around it and packaging it within a vacuole; it is also
known as &quot;cellular eating&quot;.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phagocytosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of endocytosis in which the cell gulps droplets of
extracellular fluid in tiny vesicles; it is also known as &quot;cellular
drinking&quot;.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pinocytosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of endocytosis in which proteins in the membrane with
specific receptor sites are exposed to the extracellular fluid, making the
transport specific to certain substances.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>receptor-mediated endocytosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>30) Answer the following about the splitting of sugar, for
three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the general term for the catabolic pathway which breaks
down glucose molecules, the first process in cellular respiration and
fermentation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glycolysis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In glycolysis, one molecule of glucose is converted into two
molecules of this compound.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pyruvate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Through the glycolysis pathway, for each molecule of
glucose, two molecules of one compound are phosphorylated from ADP, and two
molecules of another compound are reduced from NAD<sup>+</sup>. Give the full
names of these two compounds, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>adenosine triphosphate</u>; <u>nicotinamide adenine dinucleotide hydride</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Glycolysis is a ten-step pathway, involving ten enzymes. Name
the two enzymes which phosphorylate ADP to make ATP, and the two enzymes which
phosphorylate glucose from ATP, forming ADP.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phosphoglycerokinase, pyruvate kinase</u>; <u>hexokinase,
phosphofructokinase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the two intermediates in the glycolysis pathway which
have two phosphate groups attached.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fructose 1,6-biphosphate, 1,3-bisphosphoglycerate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>31) Answer the following concerning cellular respiration
after glycolysis, for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Upon entering the mitochondrion, a molecule of pyruvate is
converted into two compounds, as it reacts with Coenzyme A, and one molecule of
NAD<sup>+</sup> is reduced to NADH. Name these two compounds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>acetyl CoA, carbon dioxide</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the cycle of reactions which takes place in the
mitochondrion, reducing three molecules of NAD<sup>+</sup>, reducing one
molecule of FAD, phosphorylating one molecule of ADP, and releasing two
molecules of carbon dioxide, for each molecule of acetyl CoA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Krebs</u> cycle</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Identify the following intermediates in the Krebs cycle from
their descriptions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This six-carbon molecule is formed immediately after the
addition of an acetyl CoA molecule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>citrate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This four-carbon molecule is formed immediately following
the release of Coenzyme A and the phosphorylation of ADP into ATP.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>succinate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This four-carbon molecule is formed from malate and is the
immediate precursor of citrate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oxaloacetate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>32) Identify the following terms related to the completion
of cellular respiration from their definitions, for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A series of reactions in the mitochondrion membrane that
uses FADH<sub>2</sub> and NADH molecules produced in glycolysis and the Krebs
cycle and breaks the fall of electrons to oxygen into several energy-releasing
steps instead of one explosive reaction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>electron transport chain</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The production of ATP using energy derived from the redox
reactions of an electron transport chain.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oxidative phosphorylation<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The production of ATP using the energy of hydrogen-ion
gradients created by the electron transport chain to phosphoylate ADP into ATP.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chemiosmosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The potential energy stored in the form of an
electrochemical gradient, generated by the pumping of hydrogen ions across
biological membranes during chemiosmosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>proton-motive force<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A cluster of several membrane proteins found in the
mitochondrial cristae that use the energy of a hydrogen-ion concentration
gradient to make ATP.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ATP synthase<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>33) Identify the following terms related to catabolic
pathways other than cellular respiration from their definitions, for ten points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A catabolic process which makes a limited amount of ATP from
glucose without an electron transport chain, oxidizing NADH back to NAD<sup>+</sup>
by some alternate mechanism.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fermentation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this type of fermentation, common in yeast, pyruvate
molecules are converted into acetaldehyde, which is then reduced to ethanol as
NADH is oxidized to NAD<sup>+</sup>.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>alcohol</u> fermentation</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this type of fermentation, common in human muscles,
pyruvate molecules are reduced to lactate as NADH is oxidized to NAD<sup>+</sup>.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lactic acid</u> fermentation</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>34) Identify the following terms related to the first of the
two processes involved in photosynthesis from their definitions, for three
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The collective name for this process, which uses solar
energy to split water, transferring the electrons and hydrogen atoms to
nicotinamide adenine dinucleotide phosphate and phosphorylating ADP to ATP.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>light</u> reactions</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In the thylakoid membrane, chlorophyll is organized along
with proteins and other small organic molecules into these systems, which can
absorb light.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>photosystems</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are two photosystems, each with a reaction-center
chlorophyll molecule named for the wavelengths at which it absorbs light. Give
the names of the reaction-centers for Photosystem I and Photosystem II,
respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>P700</u>; <u>P680</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>When P680 absorbs light, two electrons are excited and jump
to a specialized chlorophyll a molecule. The electron &quot;hole&quot; in P680
is filled by splitting water into oxygen, hydrogen atoms, and electrons. The
excited electrons then cascade down an electron transport chain consisting of
three types of electron carriers. The electrons end up filling the electron
&quot;hole&quot; in P700, which is created when it absorbs light, exciting some
of its electrons into another of the specialized chlorophyll a <span
class=GramE>molecules</span>. These electrons then fall down another electron
transport chain consisting of an iron-containing protein. At the end, an enzyme
transfers the electrons from this protein to NADP<sup>+</sup>, creating NADPH. Give
the name for the specialized chlorophyll a molecule, the three types of
electron carriers in the first electron transport chain, the iron-containing
protein, and the enzyme which transfers electrons to NADP<sup>+</sup>,
respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primary acceptor</u>; <u>plastoquinione, cytochromes, plastocyanin</u>; <u>ferredoxin</u>;
<u>NADP<sup>+</sup> reductase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>35) Answer the following about photosynthetic pigments, for
five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This blue-green pigment is the only one which can
participate directly in the light reactions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chlorophyll a</u> (prompt on just chlorophyll)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This yellow-green accessory pigment is almost identical to
chlorophyll <span class=GramE>a, but</span> has a slightly different absorption
spectrum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chlorophyll b</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Other accessory pigments are hydrocarbons of various shades
of yellow and orange, and function in photoprotection, dissipating excessive
light energy which might damage chlorophyll.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>caretenoids</u> <u><o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the two colors of light most effective for
photosynthesis, and the least effective color.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>red, blue</u>; <u>green</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>36) Identify the following terms related to the second step
in photosynthesis from their definitions, for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cycle of reactions in the chloroplast which uses nine
molecules of ATP and six molecules of NADPH produced by the light reactions to
convert three molecules of carbon dioxide to one molecule of a sugar.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Calvin</u> cycle</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The three-carbon phosphorylated sugar which is directly
produced by the Calvin cycle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glyceraldehyde-3-phosphate</u> (prompt on G3P)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The most abundant protein on Earth, which serves as an
enzyme to attach a carbon dioxide molecule to ribulose bisphosphate in the
Calvin cycle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>rubisco</u> (or ribulose bisphosphate carboxylase)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>37) Identify the following terms related to carbon fixation
from their definitions, for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A plant which uses the Calvin cycle for the initial steps
that incorporate carbon dioxide into organic material, forming a three-carbon
compound as the first stable intermediate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>C<sub>3</sub></u> plant</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A metabolic pathway that consumes oxygen, releases carbon
dioxide, generates no ATP, and decreases photosynthetic output; it usually
occurs on hot, dry, bright days when stomata close and the oxygen content in a
leaf exceeds that of carbon dioxide.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>photorespiration</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A plant which combats photorespiration by prefacing the
Calving cycle with reactions that incorporate carbon dioxide into four-carbon
compounds, the end-product of which supplies carbon dioxide for the Calvin
cycle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>C<sub>4</sub></u> plant</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In C<sub>4</sub> plants, there are two types of
photosynthetic cells. One type <span class=GramE>are</span> tightly arranged
around the veins of the leaf, and are the only type in which the Calvin cycle
occurs. The other type <span class=GramE>are</span> loosely arranged on the
leaf surface, and incorporate carbon dioxide into four-carbon sugars. Name
these two types of cells, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bundle-sheath</u> cells; <u>mesophyll</u> cells</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In C<sub>4</sub> plants, carbon dioxide is added to a
three-carbon molecule by an enzyme to form a four-carbon sugar. Name the
three-carbon sugar, the enzyme, and the four-carbon sugar, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phosphoenolpyruvate (PEP)</u>; <u>PEP carboxylase</u>; <u>oxaloacetate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This type of metabolism is used by some plants to combat
photorespiration by converting carbon dioxide that enters open stomata at night
into organic acids which release carbon dioxide for the Calvin cycle during the
day, when the stomata are closed to conserve water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>crassulacean acid metabolism</u> (prompt on CAM)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>38) Identify the following terms related to cell
communication from their definitions, for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This is a series of steps involving reception, transduction,
and response by which a cell <span class=GramE>takes action</span> based on
external signals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>signal-transduction pathway</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This type of protein is activated when a receptor protein in
the membrane is activated by a signal molecule and displaces a GDP molecule on
this protein with a GTP molecule, activating this protein, which in turn
activates enzymes which lead to a cellular response.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>G-protein</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>When activated, the cytoplasmic side of this type of
receptor protein catalyzes the transfer of phosphate groups from ATP to an
amino acid on a substrate protein.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tyrosine-kinase</u> receptor</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These channels are protein pores in the plasma membrane that
open or close in response to a chemical signal, allowing or blocking the flow
of specific ions, such as Na<sup>+</sup> or Ca<sup>2+</sup>. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ligand-gated ion channels</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to small, nonprotein, water-soluble
molecules or ions which relay signals within a cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>second messangers<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This ring-shaped molecule made from ATP is a second
messenger.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cyclic adenosine monophosphate</u> (or cyclic AMP)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This enzyme converts ATP to cyclic AMP in response to an
external signal, such as epinephrine.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>adenylyl cyclase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These two second messengers are produced by cleavage of the
phospholipids in the plasma <span class=GramE>membrane, and</span> lead to the
release of calcium from the endoplasmic reticulum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>diacylglycerol (DAG), inositol trisphosphate (IP<sub>3</sub>)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>39) Answer the following terms related to the cell cycle,
for three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to the cell's total hereditary endowment of
DNA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>genome</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>All eukaryotic cells can be classified into two categories,
reproductive <span class=GramE>cells</span> and non-reproductive cells. Give
the names and the number of chromosomes present in the human versions of each
category, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<span class=GramE><u>gametes :</u></span><u> 23</u>; <u>somatic</u> cells : <u>46</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Each chromosome duplicated in preparation for cell division
consists of two of these, which are identical copies of the chromosome's DNA
molecule. They are separated during cell division.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sister chromatids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This is the centralized region joining two sister
chromatids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>centromere</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Each chromatid has this structure of proteins and specific
sections of chromosomal DNA at the centromere. They are pulled apart during
cell division.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>kinetochores</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This assemblage of microtubules orchestrates chromosome
movement during cell division, pulling the kinetochores apart.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
mitotic <u>spindle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This structure is a double membrane across the midline of a
dividing plant cell, between which the new cell wall forms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cell plate</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>40) Answer the following about the phases of the cell cycle,
for 2.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are two major phases in the cell cycle. During the
first, which often accounts for ninety percent of the cycle, the cell grows and
copies its chromosomes. During the second, the cell divides. Name these two
phases, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>interphase</u>; <u>mitotic phase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are three phases within interphase. During the first,
the cell begins to grow. During the second, the cell continues to grow while
replicating its DNA. During the third, the cell completes its growth. Name
these three phases, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>G<sub>1</sub> (gap 1)</u>; <u>S</u>; <u>G<sub>2</sub> (gap 2)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are six phases within the mitotic phase. Identify them
from their descriptions, which are given in chronological order.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this phase, chromatin fibers condense into chromosomes. The
nucleoli disappear. Each duplicated chromosome appears as two identical sister
chromatids <span class=GramE>joined together</span>. The mitotic spindle begins
to form. The centrosomes move away from each other.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>prophase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this phase, the nuclear envelope fragments. Each of the
two chromatids of a chromosome now have developed a kinetochore, and some
microtubules attach to the kinetochores.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>prometaphase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this phase, the centrosomes have reached opposite poles. The
chromosomes convene on an imaginary plane equidistant between the two poles. The
sister chromatids of each chromosome straddle this metaphase plate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>metaphase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this phase, the paired centromeres of each chromosome
separate, liberating the sister chromatids from each other. The kinetochore
microtubules shorten, moving the chromatids to opposite poles. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>anaphase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this phase, nuclei form at the two poles of the cell. Nuclear
envelopes arise, and the chromosomes become less tightly coiled. Mitosis is
completed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>telophase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this phase, separate from mitosis, which is the
replication of the nucleus, but still in the mitotic phase, the cytoplasm is
divided, forming two new daughter cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytokinesis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In animal cells, cytokinesis initially forms this structure,
which pinches the cell in two.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cleavage furrow</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>41) Identify the following terms related to phosphorylating
enzymes from their definitions, for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An enzyme that transfers phosphate groups from ATP to a
protein.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>protein kinase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An enzyme that remove phosphate groups from proteins.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>protein phosphatase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A protein with a cyclically fluctuating concentration in the
cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cyclin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A phosphate-transferring enzyme which must be attached to a
cyclin protein to be activated.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cyclin-dependent kinase (Cdks)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The first cyclin-dependent kinase to be discovered, it
triggers the cell's passage past the G<sub>2</sub> checkpoint into M phase.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>maturation promoting factor (MPF)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>42) Identify the following terms related to cancer from
their definitions, for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mass of abnormal cells within an otherwise normal tissue.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tumor</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The process that converts a normal cell to a cancer cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transformation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of tumor in which the abnormal cells remain at the
original <span class=GramE>site, and</span> can usually be completely removed
by surgery.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>benign</u> tumor</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of tumor which is invasive and can impair the
function of organs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>malignant</u> tumor</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The spread of cancer cells beyond their original site.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>metastasis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>43) Answer the following terms related to cell divisions
which create gametes, for 2.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This type of cell division produces gametes with half the chromosome
number of the original cell. In Phase I, homologous chromosomes are separated,
while in Phase II, which is <span class=GramE>similar to</span> mitosis, sister
chromatids are separated.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>meiosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Another term for fertilization, this refers to the union of
gametes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>syngamy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to a fertilized egg.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>zygote</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>All eukaryotic cells can be classified into two categories,
depending on whether they have one or two sets of chromosomes. Name these two
categories, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>haploid</u>; <u>diploid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this process during prophase I of meiosis, the duplicated
chromosomes pair with their homologues.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>synapsis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to the four <span class=GramE>closely
associated</span> chromatids of a homologous pair.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tetrad</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This process is the reciprocal exchange of genetic material
between nonsister chromatids during synapsis of meiosis I.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>crossing over</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This X-shaped region represents homologous chromatids that
have exchanged genetic material through crossing over.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chiasma</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The typical plant life cycle consists of both a
multicellular diploid form and a multicellular haploid form. Give the name for
this life cycle, as well as the names for both the diploid and haploid stages,
respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>alternation of generations</u>; <u>sporophyte</u>; <u>gametophyte</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>44) Identify the following terms related to genetics from
their definitions, for 1 and 7/8 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A heritable feature, such as flower color, that varies among
individuals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>character</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Each variant of a character, such as a purple flower.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>trait</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The mating, or crossing, of two varieties.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hybridization</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Plants which, when they self-pollinate, have offspring of
all the same variety.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<span class=GramE><u>true-breeding</u></span><u><o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Alternative versions of a gene.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>alleles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Having a pair of identical alleles for a character.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>homozygous<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Having two different alleles for a gene.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>heterozygous</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The allele which is expressed when an organism is
heterozygous for a character.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>dominant</u> allele</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The allele which is not expressed when an organism is
heterozygous for a character.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>recessive</u> allele</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The genetic makeup of an organism, noting all its dominant
and recessive alleles</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>genotype</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The appearance of an organism, determined by the expression
of its genotype</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phenotype</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Mendel's first law, which states that allele pairs separate
during gamete formation, and then randomly re-form pairs during the fusion of
gametes at fertilization.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>law of segregation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Breeding of an organism of unknown genotype with a
homozygous recessive individual to determine the unknown genotype.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>testcross</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the names of the first three generations in a
monohybrid cross.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
