<u>P (parental), F<sub>1</sub> (first filial), F<sub>2</sub> (second filial)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>45) Answer the following related to Mendel's second law, for
ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name Mendel's second law, which states that each allele pair
segregates independently during gamete <span class=GramE>formation, and</span>
applies when genes for two traits are located on different pairs of homologous
chromosomes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>law of independent assortment</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Use the law of independent assortment to answer the
following question. Assume yellow seeds are dominant to green seeds and that
round seeds are dominant to wrinkled seeds. Cross a homozygous yellow-round
seed with a homozygous green-wrinkled seed, and then self-pollinate the F<sub>1</sub>
generation. What will be the ratio of yellow-round to green-round to
yellow-wrinkled to green-wrinkled seeds in the F<sub>2</sub> generation?</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>9:3:3:1</u> (YYRR*yyrr = YyRr for F<sub>1</sub>)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Use the law of multiplication to answer the following
question. Assume purple flowers are dominant to white flowers, yellow seeds are
dominant to green seeds, and round seeds are dominant to wrinkled seeds. A
gardener crosses pure-breeding purple-flowered, yellow-round seeded peas with
white-flowered, green-wrinkled peas. What fraction of the F<sub>2</sub>
generation are expected to be <span class=GramE>pure-breeding</span> with white
flowers and round seeds and heterozygous with regard to seed color?</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>1/32</u> (PPYYRR*ppyyrr = PpYyRr for F<span class=GramE><sub>1</sub> ,</span>
1/4 pp, 1/2 Yy, 1/4 RR in F<sub>2</sub>)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>46) Identify the following terms related to problems with
simple Mendelian genetics from their definitions, for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of inheritance in which F<sub>1</sub> hybrids have an
appearance that is intermediate between the phenotypes of the parental
varieties.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>incomplete dominance</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of inheritance in which both alleles are separately
manifest in the phenotype.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>codominance</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The ability of a gene to affect an organism in many ways.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pleiotropy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The ability of a gene at one locus to alter the phenotypic
expression of a gene at a second locus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>epistasis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An additive effect of two or more genes on a single
phenotypic quantitative character.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>polygenic</u> inheritance</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The range of phenotypic possibilities over which a genotype
may be expressed due to environmental variations.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>norm of reaction</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>47) Identify the following genetic diseases from their
descriptions, for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>It is the most common lethal genetic disease in the <span
class=GramE>US, and</span> is caused by the lack of a membrane protein that
transports chloride ion between cells and the extracellular fluid, causing a
buildup of mucus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cystic fibrosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Most common among Ashkenazic Jews, it is caused by a
dysfunctional enzyme that fails to break down brain lipids of a certain <span
class=GramE>class, and</span> causes death within a few years.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Tay-Sachs</u> disease</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The most common inherited disease among blacks, it is caused
by the substitution of one amino acid in hemoglobin, deforming red blood cells.
Those who are carriers of this disease may be more resistant to malaria.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sickle-cell</u> anemia</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>One of the few lethal diseases caused by a dominant allele,
it has no obvious effect until the individual is at least 35 years old, but
then begins an irreversible and fatal deterioration of the nervous system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Huntington's </u>disease</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>48) Identify the following terms related to the chromosomal
basis of inheritance from their definitions, for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The most common phenotype in the natural population.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>wild</u> type</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Traits that are alternatives to the wild type.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mutant</u> phenotypes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Offspring whose phenotype matches exactly matches that of
one of its parent's phenotypes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parental</u> type</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Offspring whose phenotype is different from both of its
parents' phenotypes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>recombinant</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Genes which are located on the same chromosome and therefore
tend to be inherited together.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>linked</u> genes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The location of a gene on a chromosome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>locus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An ordered list of genetic loci along a chromosome, created
by using recombination frequencies.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>linkage map</u> (prompt on genetic map)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>49) There are several different chromosomal systems which
determine the sex of an organism. In the X-Y system, males have an X chromosome
and a Y chromosome, while females have two X chromosomes. In the X-0 system,
males have just an X chromosome, while females have two X chromosomes. In the
Z-W system, males have two Z chromosomes, while females have a Z chromosome and
a W chromosome. In the haplo-diploid system, males are haploid and <span
class=GramE>females</span> diploid. Given an organism, identify which system it
uses, for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Birds</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Z-W</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Grasshoppers</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>X-0</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fish</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Z-W</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Mammals</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>X-Y</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Bees</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>haplo-diploid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fruit flies</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>X-Y</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Ants</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>haplo-diploid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Crickets</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>X-0</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Roaches</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>X-0</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>50) Answer the following related to genetic diseases, for 2
and 1/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This X-linked disorder is caused by the absence of the
protein dystrophin and is characterized by a progressive weakening of the
muscles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Duchenne <u>muscular dystrophy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This X-linked disorder is caused by the absence of a protein
required for blood clotting.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hemophilia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to the failure of a pair of homologous
chromosomes to move apart properly during meiosis I or the failure of sister
chromatids to separate during meiosis II.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nondisjunction</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to offspring with an abnormal chromosome
number, resulting from nondisjunction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aneuploidy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to the type of aneuploidy in which three
copies of a chromosome are present.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>trisomy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to organisms with more than two complete
chromosome sets.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>polyploidy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This disease is caused by trisomy of chromosome 21.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Down syndrome</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>People with this disease have an extra X chromosome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Klinefelter</u> syndrome</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>People with this disease have only one sex chromosome, an X
chromosome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Turner</u> syndrome</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This disease is caused by a deletion on chromosome 5 and is
characterized by mental retardation, a small head, and a distinctive cry.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cri du chat</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this process, certain genes are marked in each generation
in a way to distinguish whether the gene resides in a female or male, meaning
an allele can have different effects on offspring depending on whether it is
from the mother or father.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>genomic imprinting</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>Both of these</span> diseases are caused
by a deletion in chromosome 15, but have different symptoms depending on
whether the abnormal chromosome was inherited from the mother or father. Name
the disease caused by maternal inheritance and the disease caused by paternal
inheritance, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Angelman</u>; <u>Prader-Willi</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In this disease, which is also related to genomic
imprinting, the tip of an abnormal X chromosome hangs off the rest of the
chromosome by a thin thread of DNA, causing mental retardation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fragile X</u> syndrome</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>51) Identify the following terms related to DNA replication
from their definitions, for 2 and 1/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Special sites where the two strands of parental DNA form
replication bubbles, allowing replication to begin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>origins of replication</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A Y-shaped region at each end of a replication bubble where
the new strands of DNA are elongated.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>replication fork</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Enzymes which catalyze the elongation of new DNA at the
replication fork.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>DNA polymerases</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The DNA strand which is made in the natural 5' to 3'
direction, from the phosphate on the fifth carbon of one sugar molecule to the
hydroxyl group on the third carbon of another sugar molecule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>leading strand</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The DNA <span class=GramE>strand</span> which is made in the
opposite, 3' to 5', direction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lagging strand</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The series of short segments which are synthesized backwards
and then <span class=GramE>joined together</span> to form the lagging strand,
since elongation can only occur in the 5' to 3' direction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Okazaki fragments</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The enzyme which joins the Okazaki fragments into the
lagging strand.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>DNA ligase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A short stretch of preexisting RNA which DNA polymerases
elongate, necessary since DNA polymerases cannot initiate synthesis of a
polynucleotide.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primer</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The enzyme which joins RNA nucleotides to make the primer.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The enzyme which untwists the double helix at the
replication fork.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>helicase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The proteins which hold the unpaired DNA strands apart while
complementary strands are synthesized.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>single-strand binding proteins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of DNA repair mechanism in which DNA polymerase fixes
mistakes that are made during copying.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mismatch repair</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of DNA repair mechanism in which a segment of damaged
DNA is cut out and replaced.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>excision repair</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The enzyme which cuts out damaged DNA in excision repair.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nuclease</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>52) Answer the following terms related to the synthesis of
RNA from a DNA template, for 2.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the term for the synthesis of RNA on a DNA template.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transcription</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the system by which genetic instructions for a
polypeptide chain are written in the DNA as a series of constant-length words.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>triplet code</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Identify the term which denotes the base triplets in
messenger RNA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>codons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the three-letter initiation codon and the amino acid
for which this codon also codes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>AUG</u>; <u>methionine<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the three three-letter termination codons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>UAA, UAG, UGA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the enzyme which pries the two strands of DNA apart and
hooks together the RNA nucleotides as they base-pair along the DNA template.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>RNA polymerase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the region of DNA where RNA polymerase attaches and
initiates transcription.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>promoter</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the collection of proteins which mediate the binding of
RNA polymerase and the initiation of transcription.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transcription factors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Identify the common promoter DNA sequence named for its
characteristic sequence of nucleotides.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>TATA box<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><u><o:p><span style='text-decoration:none'>&nbsp;</span></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>53) Identify the following terms related to RNA modification
from their definitions, for 3.75 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The RNA strand as it is initially after synthesis from the
DNA template, before being modified.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pre-mRNA</u> or <u>primary transcript<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The guanine nucleotide which is placed on the first end of a
new messenger RNA strand which helps protect it from degradation and helps bind
ribosomes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>5' cap</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The series of 30 to 200 adenine nucleotides which is placed
on the other end of a new messenger RNA strand and which also protects it from
degradation and helps bind ribosomes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>poly(A) tail<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The regions of RNA which are eventually translated into
amino acids and expressed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>exons<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The noncoding segments of nucleic acids that lie between the
exons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>introns</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The process of removing introns from an RNA molecule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>RNA splicing</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The particles located in the nucleus and composed of RNA and
proteins, which recognize the sites for splicing.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>small nuclear ribonucleoproteins (snRNPs)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The combination of several snRNPs and proteins which
interacts with the splice sites, cutting out introns and rejoining the flanking
exons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>spiceosome</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>54) Identify the following terms related to protein
synthesis from their definitions, for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An RNA molecule that functions as an interpreter between
nucleic acid and protein language by picking up specific amino acids and
recognizing the appropriate codons in the messenger RNA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transfer RNA (tRNA)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The nucleotide triplet on one end of a tRNA molecule which
binds to a complementary codon on mRNA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>anticodon</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Organelles composed of proteins and ribosomal RNA molecules
which facilitate the coupling of tRNA anticodons with mRNA codons during
protein synthesis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ribosomes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The enzyme which joins amino acids to their respective tRNA
molecule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aminoacyl-tRNA synthetase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>There are three binding sites for tRNA on a ribosome. The
first holds the tRNA carrying the growing polypeptide chain, the second holds the
tRNA carrying the next amino acid to be added to the chain, and the third
discharges used tRNAs from the ribosome. Name these three sites, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>P (peptidyl-tRNA) site</u>; <u>A (aminoacyl-tRNA) site</u>; <u>E (exit) site</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>55) Answer the following relating to changes in the genetic
material of a cell, for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the general term for changes in the genetic material of
a cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mutations</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the term for chemical changes in just one or a few base
pairs of a single gene.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>point mutations</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Identify the type of point mutation in which one nucleotide
and its partner in the complementary DNA strand are replaced with another pair
of nucleotides.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>base-pair substitution</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Base-pair substitutions can either change the amino acid for
which the altered codon codes, or it can change the codon to a stop signal. Name
these two types of mutations, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>missense mutations</u>; <u>nonsense mutations</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Identify the type of point mutation in which the reading
frame is altered by an insertion or deletion, causing all later codons to be
read incorrectly.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>frameshift mutations</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the term for physical or chemical agents which interact
with DNA to cause mutations.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mutagens</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>56) Answer the following related to viruses, for 2 and 8/11
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Viruses are composed of a genome and a protein shell. Give the
name for the protein shell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>capsid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Some viruses have membranes cloaking their capsids. Give the
name for these membranes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>viral envelopes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the name for bacterial viruses.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bacteriophages</u> or <u>phages</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Phages may reproduce using one of two life cycles. In one,
the virus replicates within a host cell and releases lysozyme, an enzyme which
breaks down the cell's cell wall, causing the cell to burst and release the new
phages. In the other, the virus replicates without destroying the host, as its
genome becomes incorporated into the bacterial host chromosome and replicates
with the cell. Name these two cycles, respectively.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lytic</u> cycle; <u>lysogenic</u> cycle</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to the viral DNA that is within the
bacterial host's chromosome during the lysogenic cycle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>prophage<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to viral DNA that is within the nucleus of
a eukaryotic host during the lysogenic cycle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>provirus<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Some viruses, known by this term, are capable of reproducing
using either the lytic or lysogenic cycle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbnbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>temperate</u> viruses</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This is a type of RNA virus which reproduces by transcribing
its RNA into DNA, opposite the normal pattern, and then inserts the DNA into a
cellular chromosome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>retrovirus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This is the enzyme which transcribes DNA from an RNA
template.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>reverse transcriptase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These are tiny pathogenic molecules of naked circular RNA
which infect plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>viroids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>57) Viruses may contain RNA or DNA, and the nucleic acid may
be either single stranded or double stranded. Given a viral disease, identify
the type and number of strands of its nucleic acid, for 4 and 2/7 points each. For
example, if I said papilloma, you would obviously answer &quot;double-stranded
DNA&quot;. Obviously.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Polio</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>single-stranded RNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Smallpox</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>double-stranded DNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Rabies</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>single-stranded RNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Influenza</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>single-stranded RNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Roseola</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>single-stranded DNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Herpes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>double-stranded DNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Measles</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>single-stranded RNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>58) Identify the following terms related to genetic
recombination in bacteria from their definitions, for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The alteration of a bacterial cell's genotype by the uptake
of a naked, foreign DNA from the surrounding environment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transformation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The process in which phages carry bacterial genes from one
host cell to another.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transduction</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The direct transfer of genetic material between two
bacterial cells which are temporarily joined.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>conjugation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The special piece which allows a <span class=GramE>bacteria</span>
to develop pili and donate DNA during conjugation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>F factor</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A small, circular, self-replicating DNA molecule separate
from the bacterial chromosome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>plasmid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A genetic element which can replicate either as a plasmid or
as part of the bacterial chromosome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>episome</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of plasmid responsible for conferring resistance
against antibiotics.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>R plasmids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>59) Answer the following related to &quot;jumping
genes&quot;, for 3.75 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the term for a piece of DNA that can move from one
location to another in a cell's genome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transposon</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the enzyme which catalyzes transposition.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transposase<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The simplest bacterial transposons consist of only the DNA
necessary for the act of transposition, with its only gene coding for
transposase. Name these transposons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>insertion sequences<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the pair of noncoding DNA sequences, 20 to 40
nucleotides long, which bracket the transposase gene, which are recognized by
transposase as the boundaries of the transposon.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>inverted repeats</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the term for transposons which are longer than
insertion sequences, which include extra genes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>composite transposons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give the term for transposons which move within a genome by
means of an RNA intermediate, and which are the most common type of
transposons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>retrotransposons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Within five percent, what percent of the human genome is
composed of transposons?</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>10%</u> (accept 5% to 15%)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Identify the American geneticist who won a Nobel Prize at age
81 for her work with transposons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Barbara <u>McClintock</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>60) Identify the following terms related to a unit of
coordinately regulated clusters of genes from their definitions, for six points
each. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The term for a unit of genetic function common in bacteria
and phages which consists of coordinately regulated clusters of genes with
related functions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>operon</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The DNA segment in an operon which functions as a switch,
controlling access of RNA polymerase to the operon's genes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>operator</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A protein which can switch off the operator by binding and
blocking the attachment of RNA polymerase to the promoter.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>repressor</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The gene which codes for a repressor.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>regulatory gene</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A molecule which inactivates a repressor, freeing the
operator and allowing the operon's genes to be transcribed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>inducer</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>61) Identify the following terms related to the control of
genomes from their definitions, for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Proteins containing many positively charged amino acids
which bind tightly to negatively charged DNA, packing the DNA into chromatin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>histones</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The basic unit of DNA packing, consisting of a bead-like
structure of unfolded chromatin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nucleosome</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Give two terms for short sequences of nucleotides which are
repeated in series, and accounts for up to 15% of a mammal's genome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tandemly repetitive DNA, satellite DNA</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>DNA sequences which are <span class=GramE>very similar</span>
to function genes but lack the regulatory sequences, such as promoters,
necessary for gene expression.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pseudogenes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The attachment of CH<sub>3</sub> (read: C-H-3) groups to DNA
bases, which may be necessary for long-term inactivation of genes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>DNA methylation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The attachment of COCH<sub>3</sub> (read: C-O-C-H-3) groups
to histone, changing the histones' shape, and making it easier for
transcription proteins to access genes in the region.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>histone acetylation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Molecules of this protein are commonly attached to a protein
to mark it for destruction when it is no longer needed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ubiquitin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These large protein complexes recognize ubiquitin and
degrade the marked proteins.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>proteasomes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>62) Identify the following terms related to DNA technology
from their definitions, for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Enzymes which cut DNA molecules at a limited number of
specific locations.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>restriction enzymes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This enzyme seals segments of foreign DNA into strands of
DNA cut by restriction enzymes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>DNA ligase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A DNA molecule that can carry foreign DNA into a cell and
replicate there.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cloning vector</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A complete set of thousands of recombinant-plasmid clones,
each carrying copies of a <span class=GramE>particular segment</span> from the
initial genome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>genomic library</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A technique for amplifying DNA in vitro by incubating it
with special primers, nucleotides, and a specific DNA polymerase which can
withstand the heat used to separate the DNA strands.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>polymerase chain reaction</u> (prompt on PCR)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A technique to separate macromolecules <span class=GramE>on
the basis of</span> their rate of movement through a gel under the influence of
an electric field, which is determined by their size and charge.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gel electrophoresis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A hybridization technique that enables researchers to
determine the presence of certain nucleotide sequences in a sample of DNA,
allowing the comparison of DNA of different individuals or species.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Southern blotting</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A technique to find the location of a gene on a chromosome
by allowing a radioactive probe to base-pair with complementary sequences in
the denatured DNA of intact chromosomes on a microscopic slide.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>in situ hybridization</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The study of genomes and genes based on DNA sequencing.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>genomics</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>63) Identify the following terms related to genetic
development from their definitions, for 2 and 8/11 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The divergence in form and function as cells become
specialized during an organism's development, which requires that gene
expression must be controlled on a long-term basis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>differentiation<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The process that leads up to the observable differentiation
in a cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>determination</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The physical processes that <span class=GramE>actually give</span>
shape to an organism and its various parts; literally means &quot;creation of
form&quot;.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>morphogenesis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The potential of some cells to retain the zygote's ability
to form all parts of the mature organism.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>totipotent</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Substances which establish an embryo's axes and other
features of form.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>morphogens</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Genes which influence the course of early development in an
embryo and establish the axes of its body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytoplasmic determinants<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Genes which direct the formation of segments in the embryo
of some organisms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>segmentation</u> genes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Genes which specify the types of appendages and structures
which form on each segment in some organisms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>homeotic</u> genes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A 180-nucleotide sequence within a homeotic gene that
encodes the part of the protein that binds to the DNA of the genes regulated by
the protein.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>homeobox</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The structure in the pregnant uterus for nourishing a
viviparous fetus with the mother's blood supply.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>placenta</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The small, interlacing strands of tissue in the placenta
that cause the mother's blood vessels in the vicinity to rupture.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chorionic villi</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>64) Identify the following terms related to evolution from
their definitions, for two points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The study of biological diversity in an evolutionary
context.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>systematics<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The total aggregate of genes in a population at any one time.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gene pool<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A population's frequencies of alleles and genotypes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>genetic structure</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A change in the gene pool of a population over a succession
of generations.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>microevolution</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Changes in a gene pool of a small population due to chance.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>genetic drift</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Genetic drift resulting from the reduction of a population,
typically by a natural disaster, such that the surviving population is no
longer genetically representative of the original population.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bottleneck effect</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Genetic drift attributable to colonization of a new area by
a limited number of individuals from a parent population.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>founder effect</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Genetic exchange due to the migration of fertile individuals
or gametes between populations.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gene flow</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Mating between closely related partners.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>inbreeding</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of nonrandom mating in which individuals select
partners that are like themselves in certain phenotypic characters.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>assortive mating</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Differential success in reproduction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>natural selection</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A graded change in some change along a geographical axis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cline</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The relative contribution an individual makes to the gene
pool of the next generation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Darwinian fitness</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The contribution of a genotype to the next generation
compared to the contributions of alternative genotypes for the same locus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>relative fitness</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The distinction between secondary sex characteristics of
males and females.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sexual dimorphism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>65) Identify the following terms related to the origin of
species from their definitions, for 1 and 7/8 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Evolutionary change on a large scale, incompassing the
origin of new taxonomic groups.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>macroevolution</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The accumulation of changes associated with the
transformation of one species into another.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>anagenesis</u> or <u>phyletic evolution</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The budding of one or more new species from a parent species
that continues to exist.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cladogenesis</u> or <u>branching evolution</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Obstacles which impede mating between species or hinder the
fertilization of ova if members of different species attempt to mate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>prezygotic barriers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mode of speciation in which a geographical barrier
physically isolates populations and blocks gene flow.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>allopatric</u> speciation</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mode of speciation in which intrinsic factors, such as
chromosomal changes <span class=GramE>an</span> nonrandom mating, alter gene
flow.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sympatric</u> speciation</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An individual which has more than two chromosome sets, all
from a single species.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>autopolyploid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An individual which has more than two chromosome sets, from
two different species.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>allopolyploid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A region where two related populations that diverged after
becoming geographically isolated make secondary contact and interbreed where
their ranges overlap.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hybrid zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A theory of evolution advocating spurts of relatively rapid
change followed by long periods of stasis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>punctuated equilibrium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A structure which evolved in one context and became co-opted
for another function.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>exaptation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The difference in the relative rates of growth of various
parts of the body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>allometric growth</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The situation in which adults retain features that were
juvenile structures in its evolutionary ancestors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>paedomorphosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Evolutionary changes in the timing or rate of development.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>heterochrony</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The basic body design or spatial arrangement of body parts
of an organism.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bauplan</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Alteration of the bauplan.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>homeosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>66) Identify the following geological periods from important
events in the history of life that occurred during them, for 2.5 points each. The
periods are given in chronological order.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Formation of Earth. First vertebrates.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Precambrian</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Origin of most modern animal phyla; an explosion of life is
named for this era.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cambrian</u> (the Cambrian Explosion)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Origin of plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Ordovician</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>First jawed fish. Colonization of land by vascular plants
and arthropods.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Silurian</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>First amphibians and insects.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Devonian</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>First seed plants. Origin of reptiles. Extensive forests of
vascular plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Carboniferous</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Extinction of many marine and terrestrial organisms. Origins
of mammal-like reptiles and most modern insects.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Permian</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Radiation of dinosaurs, early mammals, and birds. Gymnosperms
dominate landscape.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Triassic</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Gymnosperms and dinosaurs dominate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Jurassic</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Flowering plants appear. Many groups of organisms, including
most dinosaurs, become extinct at the end of the period.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cretaceous</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Origins of many primate groups.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Tertiary</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Humans appear.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Quaternary</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>67) Identify the following terms related to phylogeny from
their definitions, for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The independent development of similarity between species <span
class=GramE>as a result of</span> their having similar ecological roles and
selection pressures.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>convergent evolution</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Similarity in characteristics resulting from a shared
ancestry.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>homology</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Similarity of structure between two species which are not
closely <span class=GramE>related;</span> a result of convergent evolution.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>analogy</u> </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An approach to taxonomy based entirely on measurable
similarities and differences in phenotypic characters, without consideration of
homology, analogy, or phylogeny.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phenetics</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A diagram representing evolutionary branches.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phylogenetic tree<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An approach to taxonomy which classifies organisms according
to the order in time that branches arose along a phylogenetic tree.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cladistic analysis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An evolutionary branch.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>clade</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A species or group of species that is closely related to the
group of species <span class=GramE>actually being</span> studied, but clearly
not as closely related as any study-group members are to each other.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>outgroup</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The mutual influence on the evolution of two different
species interacting with each other and reciprocally influencing each other's
adaptations.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coevolution<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>68) In this bonus and the thirty-one which follow, we will
construct a hierarchical outline of all life according to the three-domain
system. Identify the three domains from their descriptions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this domain are the most diverse and widespread
prokaryotes. They contain peptidoglycan in their cell walls and have only one
kind of RNA polymerase.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbnbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Bacteria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this domain are prokaryotes without peptidoglycan
in their cell walls and with several kinds of RNA polymerase. Most inhabit the
extreme environments of Earth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Archaea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>All organisms whose cells contain a nucleus and
membrane-bound organelles are members of this domain.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Eukarya</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>69) There are about a dozen groups in Domain Bacteria. Identify
the five most important from their descriptions for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This group includes three subgroups: purple bacteria, which
are photoautotrophs or photoheterotrophs with bacteriochlorophylls built into
inpocketings of the plasma membrane; chemoautotrophic bacteria, which are
free-living and symbiotic and often participate in nitrogen fixation; and
chemoheterotrophic bacteria, which include the rod-shaped enteric bacteria
which inhabit the intestinal tracts of humans.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>proteobacteria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group have relatively simple cell walls with
a large amount of peptidoglycan, and therefore give a positive result with a
popular stain test.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Gram-positive bacteria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are photoautotrophs with plantlike
photosynthesis, and usually inhabit fresh water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cyanobacteria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are helical <span class=GramE>chemoheterotrophs,
and</span> are often very long and move like corkscrews.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>spirochetes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are all intracellular parasites of
animals, and some cause blindness and STDs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chlamydias</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>70) There are three main groups of Domain Archaea. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are named for their unique form of
energy metabolism, in which hydrogen gas is used to reduce carbon dioxide to
their namesake compound. They live in swamps and marshes and are important
decomposers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>methanogens</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group live in very salty environments, such
as the Great Salt Lake and the Dead Sea.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>extreme halophiles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group thrive in <span class=GramE>very hot</span>
environments, such as hot sulfur springs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>extreme thermophiles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>71) Domain Eukarya consists of four kingdoms. Identify them
from their descriptions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This kingdom is now often split into several kingdoms rather
than viewed as a single kingdom. In traditional classification schemes,
however, this kingdom includes all unicellular eukaryotes and their relatively
simple multicellular relatives.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Protista</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This kingdom consists of multicellular eukaryotes which
carry out photosynthesis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Plantae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this kingdom are eukaryotic heterotrophs which
acquire their nutrients by absorption.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Fungi</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this kingdom are multicellular eukaryotes that
ingest other organisms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Animalia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>72) The traditional Kingdom Protista is often split into six
candidate kingdoms. Identify them from their descriptions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this candidate kingdom are mostly parasitic and
lack mitochondria. Examples include diplomonads, trichomonads, and
microsporidians.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Archaezoa<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this candidate kingdom have flagella.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Euglenozoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this candidate kingdom have cells with subsurface
cavities.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Alveolata<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this diverse candidate kingdom are characterized
by rows of fine, hairlike projections on their flagella.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Stramenopila</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This candidate kingdom consists of red algae, and most are
multicellular photoautotrophs with cell walls of cellulose and without
flagella.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Rhodophyta</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This candidate kingdom, which some consider a part of the
Kingdom Plantae, consists of green algae, and most live in freshwater, have
cell walls of cellulose, and are free-living and symbiotic.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Chlorophyta</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>73) Candidate Kingdom Euglenozoa can be divided into two
major groups. Identify them from their descriptions for fifteen points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group, which includes Euglena, are
autotrophic and have a flagellum which arises from an anterior pocket.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Euglenoids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are parasites with a single
mitochondrion and associated extranuclear DNA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Kinetoplastids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>74) Candidate Kingdom Alveolata can be divided into three
major groups. Identify them from their descriptions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group have flagella which arise from grooves
formed by internal cellulose plates. They are abundant components of
phytoplankton, and their blooms cause red tides in coastal waters.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Dinoflagellates</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are parasites whose infectious stages
have an apical complex of organelles that penetrate the host cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Apicomplexans</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group, which includes Paramecium, have two
types of nuclei, and use cilia for motility and feeding.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Ciliates</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>75) Candidate Kingdom Stramenopila can be divided into four
major groups. Identify them from their descriptions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are freshwater or marine unicellular
photoautotrophs with two-part siliceous cell walls.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Diatoms</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are mostly freshwater unicells,
usually have two flagella, and are named for their color, which results from
their accessory pigments.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Golden algae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are usually marine multicellular
photoautotrophs with cell walls of cellulose, and are named for their color,
which results from their accessory pigments. They are the largest and most
complex algae, and most seaweed belongs to this group.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Brown algae<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This group includes water molds, white rusts, and downy
mildews.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Oomycotes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>76) There are <span class=GramE>a number of</span> other
diverse types of protists. Identify these groups from their descriptions for
7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are unicellular and use pseudopodia to
move and to feed. They reproduce asexually.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>amoebas</u> or <u>rhizopods</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group, whose name means &quot;ray
foot&quot;, have a <span class=GramE>slender pseudopodia</span> called
axopodia, and most live in planktonic habitats. They include heliozoans, which
usually live in freshwater, and radiolarian, which usually live in marine
environments. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>actinopods</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group feed and move with slender,
interconnected psudopodia exuding from spirally arranged calcareous
compartments.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>forams</u> or <u>foraminiferans<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group, which can be further divided into
pasmodial and cellular subgroups, resemble fungi in appearance and lifestyle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>slime molds</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>77) Kingdom Plantae can be divided into four major
divisions. Identify them from their descriptions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division are nonvascular plants that inhabit
the land and have a gametophyte-dominated lifecycle but lack many of the
terrestrial adaptations of vascular plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Bryophyta (bryophytes)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division have tissue consisting of cells
joined into tubes that transport water and nutrients throughout the plant body,
and they have a sporophyte-dominant lifestyle and do not produce seeds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Seedless vascular</u> plants</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division are vascular plants that bear naked
seeds not enclosed in any special chambers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Gymnosperms</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division are flowering plants, which form
seeds inside a protective chamber.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Angiosperms</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>78) Bryophytes can be divided into three divisions. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group grow together in thick mats and can
accumulate to form bogs. The peat variety covers three percent of the Earth's
surface.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mosses</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are named for the resemblance of their
lobed bodies to a human organ.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>liverworts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are <span class=GramE>similar to</span>
liverworts except that their sporophytes are elongated casules that grow like horns
from the matlike gametophyte.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hornworts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>79) Seedless vascular plants can be divided into three major
divisions. Identify them from their descriptions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division include club mosses, although they
are not <span class=GramE>mosses</span>, and some species which grow on
tropical trees.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lycophytes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division are homosporous and used to be used
to scrub pots and pans.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>horsetails</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>By far the most common division of seedless vascular plants,
members of this group are trees with long compound leaves called fronds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ferns</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>80) Gymnosperms can be divided into four major divisions. Identify
them from their descriptions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division resemble palms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cycadophyta (cycads)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division have fanlike leaves that turn gold
and are deciduous in autumn, which is unusual for gymnosperms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Ginkgophyta (ginkgos)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This division consists of Weltwitschia, Gnetum, and Ephedra,
or Mormon tea, an American shrub.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Gnetophyta</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>By far the largest division of gymnosperms, members of this
group have a reproductive structure called a cone, and include pines, firs,
spruces, larches, yews, junipers, cedars, cypresses, and redwoods.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Coniferophyta (conifers)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>81) Angiosperms can be divided into two groups, depending on
whether they have one embryonic seed leaf or two. Members of the first division
include lilies, orchids, yuccas, palms, grasses, and grain crops. Members of
the second division include roses, peas, buttercups, sunflowers, oaks, and
maples. Identify these two divisions, respectively, for fifteen points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>monocotyledones (monocots)</u>; <u>dicotyledones (dicots)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>82) Kingdom Fungi may be divided into four major divisions. Identify
them from their descriptions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group, which some consider part of Kingdom
Protista, have uniflagellated spores called zoospores, absorb nutrients, and
have cell walls made of chitin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Chytridiomycota (chytrids)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group, which includes black bread mold, form
resistant dikaryotic structures during reproduction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Zygomycota (zygote fungi)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division, which includes truffles, produce
spores in saclike asci.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Ascomycota (sac fungi)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this division have long-lived dikaryotic mycelia
and a transient diploid <span class=GramE>stage, and</span> are important
decomposers of wood.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Basidiomycota (club fungi)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>83) Fungi may also be classified according to their way of
life. Identify the following classifications from their descriptions for 7.5
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are rapidly growing, asexually
reproducing fungi. Examples include Penicillium and cheese fermenters.</p>
