<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>molds</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group are unicellular fungi that inhabit
liquid or moist habitats, including plant sap and animal tissues, and usually
reproduce by cell division or budding. They are often used to make bread rise
and alcohol ferment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>yeasts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term <span class=GramE>actually refers</span> not to an
individual fungal species, but to a symbiotic association of millions of
photosynthetic microorganisms held in a mesh of fungal hyphae. The mesh usually
includes green algae or cyanobacteria and <span class=GramE>a</span> ascomycete
fungus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lichens</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This term refers to mutualistic associations of plant roots
and fungi.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mycorrhizae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>84) Kingdom Animalia can be divided into fifteen phyla. Identify
them from their descriptions for two points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples or the common name.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum are aquatic and have a porous
skeleton composed of fibrous material or siliceous or calcareous spicules, and
often form irregularly shaped colonies attached to an underwater surface.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: sponges</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Porifera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have radial symmetry, a
gastrovascular cavity, and tentacles with stinging cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: jellyfish, corals, anemones</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cnidaria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum are marine and possess rows of
ciliary plates and adhesive colloblasts.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: comb jellies</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Ctenophora</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum are dorsoventrally flattened
acoelomates and are often parasites.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: flatworms, including planarians, blood flukes and
tapeworms</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Platyhelminthes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have jaws and a crown of cilia. Although
smaller than most protists, they have a complete digestive track.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: rotifers</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Rotifera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Among the most widespread of all animals, members of this
phylum have cylindrical, unsegmented bodies with tapered ends.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: roundworms, including hookworms, pinworms, and <i>Trichinella
spiralis</i>, which causes trichinosis</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Nematoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have bodies like flatworms but have a
small fluid-filled sac that some think is homologous to the body cavity of
protostomes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: proboscis worms or ribbon worms</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Nemertea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have a horseshoe-shaped or circular
fold of the body wall called a lophophore which bears ciliated tentacles that
surround the mouth. They are colonial and resemble mosses.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: sea mats</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Bryozoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum also have a lophophore and are
tube-dwelling marine worms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: phoronids</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Phoronida</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum also have a lophophore, live attached
to a stalk, and have a <span class=GramE>shell like</span> clams except that
the shell halves are dorsal and ventral rather than lateral.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: lamp shells</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Brachiopoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have a muscular foot, a mass
containing most of the internal organs, and a fold of tissue that often
secretes a shell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: snails, slugs, clams, oysters, squids, octopusus</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Mollusca</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have an elongated, cylindrical,
segmented body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: segmented worms, including earthworms and leeches</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Annelida</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have regional segmentation, jointed
appendages, and an exoskeleton.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: spiders, scorpions, ticks, mites, millipedes,
centipedes, insects, crabs, lobsters, crayfish, shrimp</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Arthropoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum are sessile or slow-moving, have
radial symmetry as adults, and have an endoskeleton of hard calcareous plates.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: sea stars (starfish), sea urchins</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Echinodermata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this phylum have a nerve cord, pharyngeal slits,
and usually a muscular postanal tail.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: sea squirts, salamanders, lizards, eagles, cows,
humans</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Chordata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>85) Phylum Cnidaria can be divided into three classes. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are usually marine, go through both
the polyp and medusa stages, and the polyp stage is often colonial.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: Portuguese man-of-war, hydras, Obelia, some corals</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Hydrozoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are marine and <span class=GramE>free-swimming,
and</span> have a reduced polyp stage.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: jellies, sea wasps, sea nettles</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Scyphozoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are marine, sessile, and often
colonial, and have no medusa stage.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: sea anemones, most corals, sea fans</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Anthozoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>86) Phylum Platyhelminthes can be divided into four classes.
Identify them from their descriptions for 7.5 points each. You will receive
half credit if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are usually marine, are predators and
scavengers, and have a ciliated body surface.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: planarians</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Turbellaria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are marine or freshwater parasites,
starting infection, usually of fish, with a ciliated larva.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: monogeneans</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Monogenea<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are parasites of vertebrates, have two
suckers, and have life cycles which usually include an intermediate host.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: blood flukes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Trematoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are parasites of vertebrates, attach
their scolex to a host, have proglottids which produce eggs and then break off,
have no head or digestive system, and have a life cycle with one or more
intermediate hosts.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: tapeworms</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cestoidea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>87) Phylum Mollusca can be divided into four classes. Identify
them from their descriptions for 7.5 points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are marine with an eight-plate shell,
a foot used for locomotion, and a reduced head.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: chitons</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Polyplacophora</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have an asymmetric body, usually with
a coiled shell, a foot used for locomotion, and radula.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: snails, slugs</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Gastropoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have a flattened shell with two
valves, a reduced head, and paired gills.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: clams, mussels, scallops, oysters</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Bivalvia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are marine, have a head surrounded by
grasping tentacles, usually with suckers, and move by jet propulsion.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: squids, octopuses, chambered nautiluses</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cephalopoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>88) Phylum Annelida can be divided into three classes. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have a reduced head and setae but no
parapodia.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: earthworms</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Oligochaeta</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are tube-dwelling and <span
class=GramE>free-living, and</span> have a well-developed head and parapodia
with setae on each segment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: fanworms</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Polychaeta<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have suckers at both ends of a
flattened body with a reduced coelom and are <span class=GramE>segmented, but</span>
have no setae.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: leeches</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Hirudinea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>89) Phylum Arthropoda can be divided into five classes. Identify
them from their descriptions for six points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have a body with one or two main parts
and have six pairs of appendages, including four pairs of walking legs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: spiders, scorpions, ticks, mites</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Arachnida</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are herbivorous, have a distinct head
bearing antennae and chewing mouthparts and a segmented body with two pairs of
walking legs per segment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: millipedes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Diplopoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are carnivorous, have a distinct head
with large antennae and three pairs of mouthparts, poison claws, and one pair
of walking legs per body segment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: centipedes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Chilopoda</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have a three-part body, antennae,
three pairs of wings, and usually two pairs of wings.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: beetles, ants, fleas, bees, crickets, flies</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Insecta</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are mostly marine, have antennae, and
have three or more pairs of legs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: crabs, lobsters, crayfish, shrimp</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Crustacea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>90) Class Insecta can be divided into twenty-six orders.
Identify them --- just kidding, we <span class=GramE>won't</span> go through
all of them, but identify the following eight important orders from their
descriptions for 3.75 points each. You will receive half credit if you need
examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are wingless ectoparasites with
sucking mouthparts, reduced eyes, a small flattened body, legs with clawlike
tarsi for clinging to skin, and undergo incomplete metamorphosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: sucking lice</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Anoplura</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have two pairs of winds, an armored
exoskeleton, biting and chewing mouthparts, and undergo complete metamorphosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: beetles</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Coleoptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have one pair of wings and balancing
organs called halteres, have sucking, piercing, or lapping mouthparts, and
undergo complete metamorphosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: flies, mosquitoes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Diptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have two pairs of membranous wings, a
mobile head, chewing or sucking mouthparts, a posterior stinging organ on
females, are often social, and undergo complete metamorphosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: ants, bees, wasps</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Hymenoptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have two pairs of membranous wings,
chewing mouthparts, are highly social, and undergo incomplete metamorphosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: termites</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Isoptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have two pairs of wings covered with
tiny scales and a <span class=GramE>long coiled</span> tongue for sucking, and
undergo complete metamorphosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: butterflies, moths</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Lepidoptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have two pairs of wings, biting and
chewing mouthparts, and undergo incomplete metamorphosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: crickets, roaches, grasshoppers, mantids</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Orthoptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are wingless and laterally compressed,
and adults are bloodsuckers on birds and mammals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: fleas</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Siphonaptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>91) Phylum Chordata can be divided into three subphyla. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples or the common name.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this subphylum are usually sessile marine animals
that adhere to rocks, docks, and boats. Seawater enters them through a siphon,
passes through the pharyngeal slits into a chamber called the atrium, and exits
through an atriopore.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: tunicates, such as sea squirts</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Urochordata<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this subphylum are small marine animals which
wriggle backward in the sand, trapping food particles in a mucous net secreted
across the pharyngeal slits.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: lancelets</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cephalochordata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this subphylum have a backbone.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: frogs, turtles, crows, bears</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vertebrata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>92) Subphylum Vertebrata can be divided into two
superclasses. Identify them from their descriptions for fifteen points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this superclass are jawless vertebrates with
cartilaginous skeletons and rasping tongues. Examples include lampreys and
hagfishes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Agnatha</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this superclass are vertebrates with hinged jaws
and paired appendages. It includes all extant vertebrates except lampreys and
hagfishes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Gnathostomata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>93) Superclass Agnatha can be divided into two classes. Identify
them from their descriptions for fifteen points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are marine scavengers with a mouth
surrounded by short <span class=GramE>tentacles, and</span> have no larval
stage. It includes hagfishes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Myxini</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have a mouth surrounded by an adhesive
sucker. Larvae are suspension-feeders while adults are parasitic or nonfeeding.
It includes lampreys.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cephalaspidomorphi</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>94) Superclass Gnathostomata can be divided into six
classes. Identify them from their descriptions for five points each. You will
receive half credit if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are cartilaginous fishes. They have
gills and may give birth or lay eggs, and they have a lateral line system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: sharks, skates, rays, chimaeras</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Chondrichthyes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are bony fishes. They usually have
gills, lay eggs, and have a swim bladder.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: bass, trout, perch, tuna</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Osteichthyes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class have an aquatic larval stage
metamorphosing into a terrestrial adult stage. They may give birth or lay eggs,
and breath through lungs and/or skin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: salamanders, newts, frogs, caecilians</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Amphibia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are terrestrial tetrapods with scaly
skin. They breathe through lungs and either give birth or lay amniotic shelled
eggs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: snakes, lizards, turtles, crocodiles</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Reptila</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are tetrapods with feathers. Their
forearms are modified as wings, they breathe through lungs, are endothermic,
and lay shelled amniotic eggs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: owls, sparrows, penguins, eagles</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Aves</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this class are tetrapods which usually give birth
and nourish young from mammary glands. They have hair, a diaphragm that
ventilates lungs, are endothermic, and an amniotic sac.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: platypuses, kangaroos, deer, rats, humans</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Mammalia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>95) Class Amphibia can be divided into three orders. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order retain their tails as adults. Some are
entirely aquatic, but others live on land.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: salamanders</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Urodeles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order lack tails as adults, and have
features, such as powerful hind legs, for moving on land.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: frogs</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Anurans</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are legless and nearly <span
class=GramE>blind, and</span> resemble earthworms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: caecilians</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Apodans</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>96) Class Reptilia can be divided into three extant orders. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each. You will receive half credit
if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have a hard shell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: turtles</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Chelonia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have a scaly, elongated body and live
on land.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: lizards, snakes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Squamata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order spend most of their time in water and
are among the largest living reptiles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: crocodiles, alligators</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Crocodilians</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>97) Class Aves can be divided into twenty-eight orders. Identify
these seventeen important orders from their descriptions for 1 and 13/17 points
each. You will receive half credit if you need examples. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are running birds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: ostrich</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Struthioniformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are web-footed marine birds with
tubular nostrils.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: albatrosses, shearwaters</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Procellariiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have flipper-like wings for propulsion
underwater, webbed feet short and stout, stance upright, and short and dense
feathers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: penguins</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Sphenisciformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are water birds with all 4 toes
webbed, bill hooked or straight and sharply pointed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: pelicans, tropic birds</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Pelecaniformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are web-footed birds with broad bills
containing fine plates or lamellae, or are large-footed marsh birds with
chicken-like bills</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: waterfowl, screamers</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Anseriformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are web-footed birds with long legs,
long necks, bent bills with lamellae, and much pink or red in the plumage.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: flamingos</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Phoenicopteriformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are long-legged wading birds with long
bills and unwebbed feet</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: herons, storks, ibises</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Ciconiiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are diurnal raptors with hooked beaks,
long talons, and short or <span class=GramE>very long</span> legs or
carrion-eating birds with weaker claws and tearing bills.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: hawks, falcons, vultures, condors</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Falconiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are terrestrial or arboreal
chicken-like birds with strong, scratching feet and short, rounded wings.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: grouse, pheasants, quail, turkeys</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Galliformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This order includes three suborders. Charadrii are waders,
Lari are web-footed dense-plumaged water birds, and Alcae are dense-plumaged,
web-footed marine birds and are wing-propelled divers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: plovers, sandpipers, gulls, auks</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Charadriiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are fast-flying birds with pointed
wings and weak bills, which feed on seeds and fruit.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: sand grouse, pigeons, doves, dodoes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Columbiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are often brightly colored,
strong-flying birds with very stout, hooked bills and zygodactyl feet</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: parrots, lories, cockatoos</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Psittaciformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are long-tailed birds with zygodactyl
feet</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: cuckoos, roadrunners</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cuculiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are nocturnal raptorial birds with
hooked beaks, strong talons, and soft plumage.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: owls</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Strigiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are rapid-flying birds that feed on
the wing on insects and nectar.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: swifts, hummingbirds</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Apodiformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are zygodactyl, hole-nesting birds
which eat insects and fruit.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: woodpeckers, toucans</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Piciformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This order is a large, complex assemblage of perching birds,
which contains more than half of the known species of birds</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: larks, swallows, crows</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Passeriformes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>98) Class Mammalia can be divided into three major groups. Identify
them from their descriptions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group lay eggs. Examples include platypuses
and echidnas.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Monotremes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The embryonic development of members of this group is
completed in a marsupial pouch. Examples include kangaroos, opossums, and
koalas.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Marsupials</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this group have a placenta. It includes all other
mammals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Eutherian</u> mammals</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>99) Identify the following important orders of Eutherian
mammals from their descriptions for 2.5 points each. You will receive half
credit if you need examples.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order possess hooves with an even number of
toes on each foot and are herbivorous.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: sheep, pigs, cattle, deer, giraffes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Artiodactyla</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order possess shart, pointed canine teeth
and molars for shearing, and are carnivorous.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: dogs, wolves, bears, cats, weasels, otters, seals,
walruses</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Carnivora</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are marine with fish-shaped bodes,
paddlelike forelimbs and no hind limbs, and have a thick layer of insulating
blubber.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: whales, dolphins, porpoises</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Cetacea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are adapted for flying and posses a
broad skinfold that extends from elongated fingers to body and legs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: bats</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Chiroptera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have reduced or no teeth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: sloths, anteaters, armadillos</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Edentata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are insect-eating mammals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: moles, shrews, hedgehogs</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Insectivora</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order possess chisel-like incisors and long
hind legs adapted for running and jumping.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: rabbits, hares, pikas</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Lagomorpha</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order <span class=GramE>posses</span> hooves
with an odd number of toes on each foot and are herbivorous.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: horses, zebras, tapirs, rhinoceroses</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Perissodactyla</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have opposable thumbs, forward-facing
eyes, and a well-developed cerebral cortex, and are omnivorous.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: lemurs, monkeys, apes, humans</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Primates</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order have a long, muscular trunk, thick,
loose skin, and upper incisors elongated as trunks.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: elephants</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Proboscidea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order possess chisel-like, continuously
growing incisor teeth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Examples: squirrels, beavers, rats, porcupines, mice</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Rodentia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Members of this order are aquatic herbivores and possess
finlike forelimbs and no hind limbs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Example: sea cows or manatees</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Sirenia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>100) Identify the following terms related to prokaryotes
from their definitions for 2 and 8/11 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A material composed of polymers of modified sugars
cross-linked by short polypeptides and which composes bacterial cell walls.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>peptidoglycan</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Movement toward or away from a stimulus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>taxis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The region in a prokaryotic cell in which DNA is
concentrated.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nucleoid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Resistant cells formed by some prokaryotes to withstand
harsh conditions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endospores</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Decomposers that absorb their nutrients from dead organic
matter.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>saprobes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Organisms that absorb their nutrients from the body fluids
of living hosts.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parasites</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A sticky, protective layer outside the cell wall of some
prokaryotes that enables them to adhere to their substrate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>capsule</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Surface appendages in some bacteria that functions in
adherence and the transfer of DNA during conjugation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pili</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Photosynthetic bacteria capable of making organic compounds
from water and carbon dioxide, formerly known as blue-green algae.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cyanobacteria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Pathogenic substances secreted by prokaryotes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>toxins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Chemicals that inhibit the growth of other microorganisms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>antibiotics</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>101) Prokaryotes can be classified into four groups
according to how they obtain energy and carbon. Identify these groups from
their descriptions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They obtain energy from light and carbon from carbon
dioxide.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>photoautotrophs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They obtain energy from inorganic chemicals such as hydrogen
sulfide, ammonia, or ferrous ions, and carbon from carbon dioxide.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chemoautotrophs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They obtain energy from light and carbon from organic
compounds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>photoheterotrophs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They obtain both energy and carbon from organic compounds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chemoheterotrophs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>102) Prokaryotes can also be classified into three groups
according to the effect of oxygen on their growth. Identify these groups from
their descriptions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They require oxygen for cellular respiration and cannot live
without it.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>obligate aerobes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They are poisoned by oxygen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>obligate anaerobes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They will use oxygen if present but can also grow by
fermentation in an anaerobic environment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>facultative anaerobes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>103) Identify the following terms related to relationships
between organisms of different species from their definitions for six points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for ecological relationships between
organisms of different species that are in direct contact.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>symbiosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A symbiont which is much larger than its partner.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>host</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of symbiosis in which both symbionts benefit.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mutualism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of symbiosis in which one symbiont benefits while
neither helping nor harming the other.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>commensalism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of symbiosis in which one symbiont benefits at the
expense of the other.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parasitism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>104) Identify the following terms related to protists for
2.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Protists which are animal-like in that they ingest their
food.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>protozoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Protists which are plant-like in that they are
photosynthetic.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>algae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Resistant cells formed by many protists that can survive
harsh conditions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cysts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Communities of mostly microscopic organisms that drift
passively or swim weakly near the water surface.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>plankton</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tiny infectious apicomplexan cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sporozoites</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Dead organic matter on which some protists feed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>detritus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A seaweed body that is plant-like but lacks true roots,
stems, and leaves.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thallus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A rootlike structure which anchors a thallus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>holdfast</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A stemlike structure on a thallus which supports leaflike
blades.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stipe</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The fusion of structurally similar gametes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>isogamy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The fusion of structurally distinct gametes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>anisogamy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of anisogamy in which a flagellated sperm fertilizes
a nonmotile egg.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oogamy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>105) Identify the following terms related to seedless plants
from their definitions for 2.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A waxy coating on leaves which helps prevent excessive water
loss.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cuticle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The substance that hardens the cell walls of woody tissues
in many plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lignin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Structures in which the gametes of seedless plants develop.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gametangia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The male gametangia.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>antheridium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The female gametangia.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>archegonium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The structure in which seedless plants produce haploid
spores via meiosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sporangium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A plant which produces a single type of spore.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>homosporous</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A plant which produces two types of spores.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>heterosporous</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Spores which develop into female gametophytes bearing
archegonia.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>megaspores</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Spores which develop into male gametophytes bearing
antheridia.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>microspores</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Plants that use another organism as a substratum but are not
parasites.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>epiphytes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Leaves that are specialized for reproduction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sporophylls</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>106) Identify the following terms related to the
reproductive structure of an angiosperm from their definitions for 1 and 3/7
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for the reproductive structure of an
angiosperm</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>flower</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The whorl of modified leaves that encloses and protects a
flower bud before it opens.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sepal</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The usually colorful part of a flower which aids in
attracting insects and other pollinators.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>petals</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An immature male gametophyte that develops within flowers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pollen<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The pollen-producing male reproductive organ of a flower.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stamen</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The stalk of the stamen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>filament</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The terminal sac at the end of the filament, where pollen is
produced.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>anther</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A sporophyte embryo packaged along with a food supply within
a protective coat.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>seed</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The triploid tissue of a seed which is rich in starch and
other food reserves.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endosperm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The seed leaves of an angiosperm embryo.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cotyledons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The absorption of water by a dry seed due to its low water
potential.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>imbibition<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A structure consisting of a nucellus, integuments, and
megaspores, which develop into seeds when fertilized.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ovules</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The female reproductive organ of a flower.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>carpel</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The portion at the base of a carpel in which the ovules
reside.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ovary</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mature ovary that protects dormant seeds and aids in their
disposal.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fruit</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>The thickened wall of a fruit,</span> made
from the ovary.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pericarp<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A fruit derived from a single ovary, such as cherries and
soybeans.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>simple fruit</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A fruit that results from a single flower that has several
carpels, such as bluberries.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aggregate fruit</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A fruit that develops from a group of flowers in a tight
cluster, called an inflorescence, such as a pineapple.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>multiple fruit<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The portion of the carpel which leads to the ovary.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>style</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The sticky end of the carpel which receives pollen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stigma</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>107) Identify the following terms related to transport in
plants from their definitions for three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of tissue consisting of cells joined into tubes that
transport water and nutrients throughout the plant body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vascular</u> tissue</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The vascular tissue which conveys water and dissolved
minerals upward from roots into the shoots.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>xylem</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The vascular tissue which transports food made in mature
leaves to the roots and to parts of the shoot system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phloem</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The coupling of the downhill diffusion of one substance to
the uphill transport of another against its own concentration gradient.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cotransport</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The continuum of cytoplasm connected by plasmodesmata
between cells, through which certain molecules can be transported.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>symplast</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The nonliving continuum formed by the extracellular pathway
provided by the continuous matrix of cell walls.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>apoplast</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The movement of a fluid driven by pressure.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bulk flow</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A waxy belt in the wall of each endodermal cell which is
impervious to water and dissolved minerals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Casparian strip</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Exudation of water droplets from a plant, due to an upward
push of xylem sap called root pressure.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>guttation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The transport via phloem of food in a plant.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>translocation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>108) Identify the following terms related to roots from
their definitions for 2 and 4/13 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A root system consisting of one large, vertical root that
produces many smaller lateral roots.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>taproot</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tiny appendages which drastically increase the surface area
of roots.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>root hairs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Roots which arise aboveground from stems or even leaves.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>adventitious</u> roots</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Embryonic plant tissue in the tips of roots that supply
cells for the plant to grow in length.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>apical meristem</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The structure at the root tip which physically protects the
delicate meristem as the root elongates.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>root cap</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A population of cells near the center of the apical meristem
which divide much more slowly that the other meristematic cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>quiescent center</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The region of the root consisting of the apical meristem and
the primary meristems.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>zone of cell division</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The region of the root in which cells elongate to more than
ten times their original length.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>zone of elongation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The region of the root where cells complete their
differentiation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>zone of maturation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The central vascular cylinder in roots where xylem and
phloem are located.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stele</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The core of the central vascular cylinder of monocot roots,
consisting of parenchyma cells, which are ringed by vascular tissue.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pith</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The region of the root between the stele and epidermis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cortex</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The innermost layer of the cortex, consisting of a cylinder
one cell thick that forms the boundary with the stele.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endodermis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>109) Identify the following terms related to stems from
their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The points on a stem where leaves are attached.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nodes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The stem segments between nodes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>internodes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The angle between a stem and a leaf, which has the potential
to form a branch shoot.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>axillary bud</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The tip of a young stem.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>apex</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The collection of leaves at the apex.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>terminal bud</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Strands of vascular tissue in the stem.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vascular bundles<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>110) Identify the following terms related to leaves from
their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The stalk of a leaf.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>petiole</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The non-stalk part of a leaf.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>blade</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>The ground tissue of a leaf,</span> sandwiched
between the upper and lower epidermis, which contains parenchyma cells
specialized for photosynthesis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mesophyll</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three basic types of leaf base on the arrangement
of leaflets.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>simple, compound, doubly compound</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>111) Answer the following related to the different types of
plant cells and tissues for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Relatively unspecialized plant cells with thin, flexible
primary walls.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parenchyma</u> cells</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the cells with unevenly thickened primary walls which
provide support to parts of the plant that are still growing.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>collenchyma</u> cells</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the cells used for support which have secondary walls
hardened with lignin and may be dead at functional maturity. There are two
types, fiber cells and sclereids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sclerenchyma</u> cells</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the two types of water-conducting xylem cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tracheids, vessel elements<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the food-conducting cells of phloem.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sieve-tube members</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three types of plant tissues.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>dermal (or epidermal), vascular, ground</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>112) Identify the following terms related to plant growth
from their definitions for 2 and 8/11 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Plants which complete their life cycle in a single year or
less.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>annuals</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Plants which live for many years.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>perennials</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Perpetually embryonic tissues in a plant's regions of
growth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>meristems</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of growth in which the plant elongates.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primary growth</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of growth in which roots and shoots thicken.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>secondary growth</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cylinders of dividing cells along the roots and shoots,
which is responsible for secondary growth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lateral meristems</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Lateral meristems which produce secondary xylem, or wood,
and phloem.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vascular cambium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Lateral meristems which produce a tough, thick covering for
stems and roots that replaces the epidermis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cork cambium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Layers of cork plus the cork cambium</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>periderm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>All tissues external to the vascular cambium.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bark</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Spongy regions in the bark which allow exchange of gases for
cellular respiration.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lenticels</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>113) Identify the following terms related to soil from their
definitions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Decomposing organic material formed by the action of
bacteria and funi on dead organisms, feces, fallen leaves, and other organic
refuse.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>humus<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mixture of rock particles, living organisms, and humus on
ground level.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>topsoil</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Distinct soil layers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>horizons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fertile soils made of roughly equal amounts of sand, silt,
and clay.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>loams<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>114) Identify the following terms related to cloning from
cuttings from their definitions for ten points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The mass of dividing, undifferentiated cells at the cut end
of the shoot.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>callus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The plant that provides the root system in a grafting.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stock</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The twig that is grafted onto the stock.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>scion</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>115) Identify the following plant hormones from their
descriptions for 2 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>It stimulates stem elongation and is produced in the embryo
of a seed, meristems of apical buds, and in young leaves.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>auxin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They affect root growth and differentiation and are produced
in the roots.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytokinins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They promote seed and bud germination, stem elongation, and
leaf growth, and are produced in the meristems and the embryo.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gibberellins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They inhibit growth and close stomata during water stress,
and are produced in leaves, stems, roots, and green fruit.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>abscisic acid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>It promotes fruit ripening and can either promote or inhibit
<span class=GramE>growth, and</span> is found in the tissues of ripening
fruits.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ethylene</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They trigger defense responses against pathogens and are
found in cell walls.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oligogaccharins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They are required for nomral growth and development and are
found in seeds, fruits, shoots, leaves, and floral buds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>brassinosteroids</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>116) Identify the following terms related to the orientation
of plant growth from their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for growth responses that result in
curvature of whole plant organs toward or away from stimuli.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tropism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tropism in response to light.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phototropism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tropism in response to gravity.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gravitropism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tropism in response to touch.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thigmotropism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The developmental response to mechanical perturbation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thigmomorphogenesis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A physiological response to day length, such as flowering in
plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>photoperiodism<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>117) Identify the following terms related to fungi from
their definitions for 3.75 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Minute threads composed of tubular walls surrounding plasma
membranes and cytoplasm which make up the body of fungi.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hyphae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An interwoven mat of hyphae which serves as the feeding
network of a fungus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mycelium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cross-walls which divide the cells in a fungus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>septa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fungi which are not divided by septa, and instead consist of
a continuous cytoplasmic mass with hundreds or thousands of nuclei.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coenocytic fungi<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A strong but flexible nitrogen-containing polysaccharide
used in fungal cell walls.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chitin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Small clusters of hyphae with embedded algae, used in lichen
asexual reproduction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>soredia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fungi with no known sexual stages.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>imperfect fungi</u> or <u>deuteromycetes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Nutrient-absorbing hyphal tips which parasitic fungi use to
penetrate the tissues of their host.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>haustoria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>118) Identify the following terms related to animal
development from their definitions for three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A succession of mitotic cell divisions undergone by a
zygote.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cleavage</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A multicellular stage during the development of most
animals, in which many animals take the form of a hollow ball.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>blastula</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A stage in which layers of embryonic tissues that will
develop into adult body parts are produced.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gastrula</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Concentric layers formed by the process of gastrulation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>germ layers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The outermost of the three primary germ layers in an <span
class=GramE>animal embryos</span>, which gives rise to the outer covering.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ectoderm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The innermost of the three primary germ layers that lines
the developing digestive tube.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endoderm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The middle of the three primary germ layers that develops
into the notochord and most of the circulatory system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mesoderm<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A sexually immature form morphologically distinct from the
adult stage.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>larva</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The resurgence of development in an animal larva that
transforms it into a sexually mature adult.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>metamorphosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An evolutionary trend toward the concentration of sensory
equipment on the anterior end.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cephalization</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>119) Identify the following terms related to animal body
plans from their definitions for 2 and 8/11 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Animals, namely the sponges, that lack true tissues.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parazoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Animals that do have true tissues.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>eumetazoa</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Animals whose body parts are arranged like spokes on a
wheel.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Radiata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Animals whose body parts are arranged such that exactly one imaginary
cut would divide the animal into mirror-image halves.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Bilateria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A body cavity lined by mesoderm.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coelom</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Animals with solid bodies, with no cavity between the
digestive tract and outer body wall.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>acoelomates</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Animals with a body cavity that is not entirely lined by
mesoderm.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pseudocoelomates</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Animals with a true body cavity.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coelomates</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The opening of the archenteron in the gastrula.</p>
