<p class=MsoNormal>126) Identify the following terms related to collections of
animal cells from their definitions for 3.75 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for groups of cells with a common structure
and function.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tissues</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tissue that covers the outside of the body and lines organs
and cavities within the body. It may be simple, having a single layer of cells,
or stratified, having multiple tiers of cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>epithelial</u> tissue</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A specialized form of loose connective tissue that stores
fat.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>adipose</u> tissue</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of flexible connective tissue with an abundance of
collagenous fibers embedded in chondrin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cartilage</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mineralized connective tissue.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cells which make bone.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>osteoblasts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The repeating units in the structure of hard mammalian bone.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Haversian systems</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The internal environment of vertebrates, consisting of the
fluid filling the spaces between cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>interstitial fluid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>127) Identify the following vitamins from their functions in
the human body for 1.5 points each. If you need symptoms of their deficiency,
you will receive two-thirds credit. If you need some major dietary sources, you
will receive one-third credit. For an additional 21/26 point each, also tell
whether each is water-soluble or fat-soluble.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Coenzyme used in removing carbon dioxide from organic
compounds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: beriberi</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: pork, legumes, peanuts, whole grains</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin B<sub>1</sub></u> or <u>thiamine</u>; <u>water soluble<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Component of coenzymes FAD and FMN.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: skin lesions</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: dairy products, meats, enriched grains, vegetables</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin B<sub>2</sub></u> or <u>riboflavin</u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Component of coenzymes NAD<sup>+</sup> and NADP<sup>+</sup>.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: skin and gastrointestinal lesions,
nervous disorders</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: nuts, meats, grains</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Niacin</u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Coenzyme used in amino acid metabolism.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: irritability, convulstions, muscular
twitching, anemia</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: meats, vegetables, whole grains</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin B<sub>6</sub></u> or <u>pyridoxine</u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Component of coenzyme A</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: fatigue, numbness, tingling of hands
and feet</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: most foods</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Pantothenic acid</u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Coenzyme in nucleic acid and amino acid metabolism</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: anemia, gastrointestinal problems</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: green vegetables, oranges, nuts, legumes, whole
grains</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Folic acid</u> or <u>folacin</u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Coenzyme in nucleic acid metabolism, needed for maturation
of red blood cells</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: Anemia, nervous system disorders</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: meats, eggs, dairy products</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin B<sub>12</sub></u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Coenzyme in the synthesis of fat, glycogen, and amino acids</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: scaly skin, neuromuscular disorders</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: legumes, other vegetables, meats</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Biotin</u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used in collagen synthesis, an antioxidant, aids in
detoxification, and improves iron absorption</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: scurvy, weakness, delayed wound
healing, impaired immunity</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: fruits and vegetables, especially citrus fruits,
broccoli, cabbage, tomatoes, green peppers</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin C</u> or <u>ascorbic acid</u>; <u>water soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Component of visual pigments, needed for maintenance of
epithelial tissues, an antioxidant, and helps prevent damage to the lipids of
cell membranes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: vision problems, dry skin</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: beta-carotene in deep green and orange vegetables
and fruits, dairy products</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin A</u> or <u>retinol</u>; <u>fat soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Aids in absorption and use of calcium and phosphorus, and
promotes bone growth</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: rickets, bone softening</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: dairy products, egg yolk, sunlight</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin D</u>; <u>fat soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An antioxidant, and helps prevent damage to the lipids of
cell membranes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: none known</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: vegetable oils, nuts, seeds</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin E</u> or <u>tocopherol</u>; <u>fat soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Important in blood clotting</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Symptoms of deficiency: defective blood clotting</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Sources: green vegetables, tea</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Vitamin K</u> or <u>phylloquinone</u>; <u>fat soluble</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>128) Identify the following minerals required by humans from
their major functions and dietary sources for three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used for bone and tooth formation, blood clotting, and nerve
and muscle function, it is found in dairy products, dark green vegetables, and
legumes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>calcium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used for bone and tooth formation, acid-base balance, and
nucleotide synthesis, it is found in dairy products, meats, and grains.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phosphorus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used as a component of certain amino acids, it is found in
proteins from many sources.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sulfur</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used for acid-base balance, water balance, and nerve
function, it is found in meats, dairy products, grains, and many fruits and
vegetables.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>potassium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used for acid-base balance, formation of gastric juice,
nerve function, and osmotic balance, it is found in table salt.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chlorine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used for acid-base balance, water balance, and nerve
function, it is found in table salt.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sodium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used as a cofactor and in ATP bioenergetics, it is found in
whole grains and green leafy vegetables.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mangnesium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used as a component of hemoglobin and of electron-carriers
in metabolism and as an enzyme cofactor, it is found in meats, eggs, legumes,
whole grains, and green leafy vegetables.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>iron</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used for maintaining tooth and probably bone structure, it
is found in drinking water, tea, and seafood.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fluorine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Used as a component of thyroid hormones, it is found in
seafood, dairy products, and salt.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>iodine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>129) Identify the following terms related to the digestive
system from their definitions for 1.25 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A complete digestive tract.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>alimentary canal</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A digestive enzyme that hydrolyzes starch and glycogen in
the mouth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>salivary amylase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The ball of food pushed into the back of the oral cavity by
the tongue.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bolus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The throat.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pharynx</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cartilaginous flap that covers the trachea when food is
swallowed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>epiglottis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The tube that conducts food from the pharynx down to the
stomach.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>esophagus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The digestive fluid that mixes with food in the stomach.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gastric juice</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The enzyme that begins the hydrolysis of proteins in the
stomach.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pepsin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>The active form of pepsin,</span> secreted
by chief cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pepsinogen</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The nutrient broth in the stomach resulting from enzyme
action on food.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>acid chyme</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The organ in which most enzymatic hydrolysis of
macromolecules and most absorption of nutrients occurs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>small intestine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for a muscular valve.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sphincter<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The sphincter at the opening between the stomach and the
small intestine which helps regulate the passage of chyme.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pyloric sphincter</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The first section of the small intestine, in which acid
chyme mixes with digestive juices from the pancreas, liver, and gallbladder.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>duodenum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the other two regions of the small intestine, which
function in the absorption of nutrients and water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>jejunum, ileum<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mixture of digestive substances produced by the liver and
stored in the gallbladder until needed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bile</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Fingerlike projections on the lining of the small intestine
which absorb nutrients.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>villi</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Microscopic appendages on the villi.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>microvilli</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The hormone which stimlates sustained secretion of gastric
juice in the stomach.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gastrin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The hormone that stimulates the pancreas to release
bicarbonate, which neutralizes acid chyme.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>secretin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The organ which food enters after leaving the small
intestine, and in which water is reabsorbed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>colon</u> or <u>large intestine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The dispensable, fingerlike extension on the cecum pouch of
the large intestine.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>appendix</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The terminal portion of the colon, where feces are stored
until eliminated.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>rectum<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>130) Identify the following terms related to the circulatory
system from their definitions for 1 and 2/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The chambers of the heart that receive incoming blood.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>atria</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The chambers of the heart that pump out blood.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ventricles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Vessels that carry blood away from the heart to organs
throughout the body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>arteries<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Microscopic blood vessels with very thin, porous walls, that
infiltrate each tissue.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>capillaries</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Small vessels that convey blood from the arteries to the
capillaries.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>arterioles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Vessels that return blood to the heart.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>veins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Small vessels that convey blood from the capillaries to the
veins.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>venules</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The circuit in double circulation in which blood goes to gas
exchange tissues where the blood picks up oxygen and returns to the left atrium
of the heart.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pulmocutaneous circuit</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The circuit in double circulation in which oxygen-rich blood
is carried to all body organs and returns to the right atrium.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>systemic circuit</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Valves of connective tissue that prevent backflow of blood
between each atrium and ventricle.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>atrioventricular valves</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The rhythmic stretching of the arteries caused by the
pressure of blood driven by the contraction of the ventricles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pulse</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The contraction phase of the cardiac cycle in which blood is
pumped.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>systole</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The relaxation phase of the cardiac cycle in which the heart
chambers fill with blood.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>diastole</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The amount of blood pumped by the left ventricle each time
it contracts.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stroke volume</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A test that measures the electrical currents produced by
cardiac impulses.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>electrocardiogram (ECG or EKG)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The single layer of flattened cells that lines the lumen of
all blood vessels.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endothelium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The hydrostatic force that blood exerts against the wall of
a vessel.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>blood pressure</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The arteries that provide oxygen-rich blood to the heart.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coronary arteries<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>131) Identify the following terms related to cardiovascular
diseases from their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A cardiovascular disease in which nervous tissue in the
brain dies <span class=GramE>as a result of</span> artery blockage.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>stroke</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The death of cardiac muscle tissue resulting from prolonged
blockages of one or more coronary arteries.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>heart attack<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A cardiovascular disease in which growths develop on the
inner walls of arteries, narrowing their bore.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>atherosclerosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The growths which develop on the artery walls in
atherosclerosis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>plaques<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of atherosclerosis in which plaques become hardened
by calcium deposits.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>arteriosclerosis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>High blood pressure.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hypertension<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>132) Identify the following terms related to blood from
their definitions for three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The liquid matrix of blood in which the cells are suspended.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>plasma</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The most numerous blood cells, also known as red blood
cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>erythrocytes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An oxygen-carrying protein in erythrocytes that contains
iron.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hemoglobin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Infection-fighting blood cells, also known as white blood
cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>leukocytes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cell fragments in blood that function in blood clotting.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>platelets</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cells in red bone marrow from which erythrocytes,
leukocytes, and platelets all develop.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pluripotent stem cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The hormone produced by the kidney that stimulates
production of erythrocytes in the bone marrow.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>erythropoietin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The inactive form of the blood-clotting plasma protein
sealant.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fibrinogen</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The active form of fibrinogen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fibrin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A clot within a blood vessel.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thrombus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>133) Identify the following terms related to the respiratory
system from their definitions for 1 and 2/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for the uptake of molecular oxygen from the
environment and the discharge of carbon dioxide into the environment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gas exchange</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Variously shaped outfoldings of the body surface specialized
for gas exchange.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gills<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The opposite flow of adjacent fluids that maximizes transfer
rates, such as blood in gills flowing in the opposite direction as water,
maximizing gas exchange.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>countercurrent exchange</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A gas exchange system in insects, consisting of branched,
chitin-lined tubes that infiltrate the body and carry oxygen directly to cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tracheal system<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tiny air tubes that branch throughout the insect body for
gas exchange.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tracheae</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The respiratory surfaces of terrestrial vertebrates, land
snails, and spiders that connect to the atmosphere by narrow tubes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lungs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The upper part of the respiratory tract.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>larynx</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cords in the larynx that produce sound when stretched.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vocal cords<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The windpipe.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>trachea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The two tubes that branch from the trachea to the lungs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bronchi</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The fine branches of the bronchi within the lungs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>bronchioles</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tiny air sacs at the end of the tiniest bronchioles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>alveoli</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The alternate inhalation an exhalation of air.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>breathing</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of lung ventilation, used by frogs, in which air is
pushed down the windpipe.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>positive pressure breathing</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of lung ventilation, used by mammals, in which air is
pulled down the windpipe like a suction pump.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>negative pressure breathing</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The sheet of skeletal muscle that forms the bottom wall of
the chest cavity and contracts to increase the volume of the lungs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>diaphragm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Tiny channels in the lungs of birds through which air flows
continuously in one direction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parabronchi</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The oxygen-storing protein present in high concentrations in
the muscles of diving mammals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>myoglobin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>134) Identify the following terms related to the immune
system from their definitions for 1.25 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Any protein that specifically recognize and help combat
viruses, bacteria, or other invaders of the body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>immunoglobulin<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Phagocytic cells that constitute sixty to seventy percent of
leukocytes and engulf and destroy invading microbes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>neutrophils</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Phagocytic cells that constitute five percent of leukocytes
and migrate into tissues, forming large macrophages which can exist for a long
time and are <span class=GramE>very effective</span> at destroying microbes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>monocytes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cells that constitute one and a half percent of leukocytes
and destroy large parasitic invaders, such as blood flukes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>eosinophils</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cells that destroy virus-infected body cells and abnormal
cells that could form tumors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>natural killer cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Antiviral proteins secreted by virus-infected cells that
induce neighboring cells to produce chemicals that inhibit viral reproduction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>interferons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cells that recognize and respond to <span class=GramE>particular
microbes</span> and foreign molecules.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lymphocytes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Lymphocytes that complete their development in the bone
marrow.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>B cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Lymphocytes that complete their development in the thymus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>T cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A foreign molecule that elicits a response by lymphocytes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>antigen</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Short-lived cells that combat an antigen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>effector cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Long-lived cells that have receptors specific for an
antigen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>memory cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An antigen-binding immunoglobulin produced by B cells that
functions as the effector in an immune response.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>antibody</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The selective proliferation and differentiation of
lymphocytes that occurs the first time the body is exposed to an antigen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primary immune response</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The faster, greater, and longer response of the body if
exposed to the same antigen at some later time.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>secondary immune response</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Cells that have receptors that bind to fragments of antigens
displayed by the body's class II major histocompatibility complex molecules.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>helper T cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Proteins or peptides secreted by helper T cells that
stimulate other lymphocytes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cytokines</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Antigens that evoke a B cell response that requires help
from helper T cells to produce antibodies.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>T-dependent antigens</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the only blood group which can be donated to any group
without clumping.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>O</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the only blood group which can receive from any group
without clumping.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>AB</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A red blood cell antigen, against which antibodies of the
IgG class are produced.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Rh</u> factor</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Hypersensitive responses to certain environmental antigens.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>allergies</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A life-threatening reaction to injected or ingested
allergens.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>anaphylactic shock</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Infections and cancers that take advantage of an immune
system in collapse.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>opportunistic diseases</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>135) Identify the following terms related to the control of an
animal's internal environment from their definitions for 2 and 4/13 points
each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The maintenance of body temperature within a range that
enables cells to function efficiently.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thermoregulation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The direct transfer of heat between molecules of the
environment and those of the body surface.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>conduction</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The transfer of heat by the movement of air or liquid past
the surface of a body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>convection</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The emission of electromagnetic waves produced by all
objects warmer than absolute zero.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>radiation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The loss of heat from the surface of a liquid that is losing
some of its molecules as gas.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>evaporation<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An organism that warms its body mainly by absorbing heat
from its surroundings.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ectotherm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An organism, such as mammals, birds, some fish, and many
insects, that derives most of its body heat from its own metabolism.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endotherm<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An increase in the diameter of superficial blood vessels,
used for cooling.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vasodilation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A decrease in the diameter of superficial blood vessels,
used to retain heat.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vasoconstriction</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A tissue in the neck and shoulders that is specialized for
rapid heat production.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>brown fat</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An alternative physiological state in which metabolism
decreases and the heart and respiratory system slow down.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>torpor</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Long-term torpor during which the body temperature is
lowered as an adaptation to winter cold and food scarcity.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hibernation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Torpor during the summer.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>estivation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>136) Identify the following terms related to water balance
and waste disposal from their definitions for 1 and 11/19 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The regulation of solute balance and the gain and loss of
water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>osmoregulation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A layer or layers of epithelial cells that regulate solute
movements.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>transport epithelium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A soluble form of nitrogenous waste excreted by mammals and
most adult amphibians.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>urea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An insoluble precipitate of nitrogenous waste that can be
excreted by land snails, insects, birds, and some reptiles with little loss of
water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>uric acid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of tubular excretory system, found in most annelids,
that has internal openings that collect body fluids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>metanephridium</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Unique excretory organs in insects that empty into the
digestive tract, remove nitrogenous wastes from the blood, and function in
osmoregulation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Malpighian tubules</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The pair of bean-shaped organs that produce urine and
regulate the composition of the blood.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>kidneys</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The artery through which blood enters the kidneys.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>renal artery</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The duct through which urine exits the kidney.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ureter</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The compartment into which the ureters empty.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>urinary bladder</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The tube through which urine leaves the body.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>urethra</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The outer of the two regions of the kidney.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>renal cortex</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The inner of the two regions of the kidney.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>renal medulla</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The functional unit of the vertebrate kidney, consisting of
a single long tubule and a ball of capillaries.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nephron</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The ball of capillaries in the nephron.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glomerulus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cup-shaped swelling at the end of the nephron's tubule.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Bowman's capsule</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A hairpin <span class=GramE>turn</span> in the nephron with
a descending limb and an ascending limb, that functions in water and salt
reabsorption.<b><o:p></o:p></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>loop of Henle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The eighty percent of nephrons that have reduced loops of
Henle and are almost entirely confined to the renal cortex.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cortical nephrons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The twenty percent of nephrons that have well-developed
loops of Henle that extend into the renal medulla.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>juxtamedullary nephrons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>137) Identify the following terms related to chemical
signals in animals from their definitions for two points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The collective name for <span class=GramE>all of</span> an
animal's hormone-secreting cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endocrine system</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Specialized nerve cells that secrete hormones.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>neurosecretory cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Peptides and proteins that function as local regulators and
must be present in the extracellular environment for many types of cells to
grow.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>growth factors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A hormone that has another endocrine gland as its target.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tropic hormones</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A hormone produced in the brain and anterior pituitary that
inhibits pain perception.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endorphin<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A hormone that lowers blood glucose levels by promoting the
uptake of glucose by most body cells and the synthesis and storage of glycogen
in the liver.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>insulin<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Clusters of endocrine cells in the pancreas that secrete
glucagon and insulin directly into the circulatory system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>islets of Langerhans</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An autoimmune disorder in which the immune system mounts an
attack on the cells of the pancreas, destroying the ability to produce insulin,
and usually occurring suddenly during childhood.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Type I diabetes mellitus</u> (prompt on partial answer)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An autoimmune disorder characterized by either a deficiency
of insulin or reduced responsiveness in target cells due to some change in
insulin receptors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Type II diabetes mellitus</u> (prompt on partial answer)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A class of hormone compounds synthesized from the amino acid
tyrosine.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>catecholamines</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of catecholamine produced by the adrenal medulla <span
class=GramE>and also</span> known as adrenaline.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>epinephrine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The other major type of catecholamine.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>norepinephrine</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Hormones which stimulate the development and maintenance of
the male reproductive system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>androgens</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The main androgen.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>testosterone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Hormones which stimulate the development and maintenance of
the female reproductive system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>estrogens</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>138) Identify the following major vertebrate endocrine
glands from the names and actions of some of the hormones they produce for 2.5
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Oxytocin, which stimulates the contraction of the uterus and
mammary gland cells; antidiuretic hormone, which promotes water retention by
the <span class=GramE>kidneys;</span> </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>posterior pituitary gland<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Growth hormone, which stimulates growth; prolactin, which
stimulates milk production; follicle-stimulating hormone, which stimulates
production of gametes; thyroid-stimulating hormone, which stimulates the
thyroid gland; luteinizing hormone, which stimulates the gonads; and
adrenocorticotropic hormone, which stimulates the adrenal cortex to secrete
glucocorticoids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>anterior pituitary gland</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Triiodothyonine and thyoxine, which stimulates and maintains
metabolic processes; and calcitonin, which lowers the blood calcium level.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thyroid gland</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Parathyroid hormone, which raises the blood calcium level.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parathyroid glands</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Insulin, which lowers blood glucose level; and glucagon,
which raises blood glucose level.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pancreas</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Epinephrine and norepinephrine, which raise blood glucose
level, increase metabolic activities, and constrict certain blood vessels.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>adrenal medulla<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Glucocorticoids, which raise blood glucose level; and
mineralocorticoids, which promote reabsorption of sodium and excrete potassium
in the kidneys.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>adrenal cortex</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Androgens, which promote the development and maintenance of
the male reproductive system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>testes</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Estrogens, which promote the development and maintenance of
the female reproductive system; and progeterone, which promotes uterine lining
growth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ovaries</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Melatonin, which is involved in biological rhythms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pineal gland</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Thymosin, which stimulates T lymphocytes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thymus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the endocrine gland that produced hormones released by
the posterior pituitary and hormones that regulate the anterior pituitary
glands.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hypothalamus<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>139) Identify the following terms related to animal
reproduction from their definitions for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The separation of a parent into two or more individuals of
approximately equal size.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fission</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The process by which new individuals split off from existing
ones.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>budding</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The breaking of the body into several pieces, <span
class=GramE>some</span> or all of which develop into complete adults.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fragmentation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The regrowth of lost body parts.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>regeneration</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A process by which an egg develops without being fertilized.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>parthenogenesis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An individual which functions as both male and female,
producing eggs and sperm.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hermaphrodite</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Chemical signals released by one organism that influence the
behavior of other individuals of the same species.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pheromones</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The organs that produce gametes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gonads</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An opening to the outside shared by the digestive,
excretory, and reproductive systems.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cloaca</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>140) Identify the following terms related to animal
development from their definitions for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A theory of embryonic development proposed by Aristotle
stating that the form of an animal emerges gradually from a relatively formless
egg.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>epigenesis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A succession of mitotic cell divisions undergone by a
zygote.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cleavage</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The many small cells formed from the zygote by cleavage.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>blastomeres</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The nutrients stored in an egg.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>yolk</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The pole of an egg containing a high concentration of yolk.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vegetal pole</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The pole of an egg containing a low concentration of yolk.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>animal pole</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The formation of a two-layered, cup-shaped embryo from a
blastula.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gastrulation</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The formation of organs in an embryo.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>organogenesis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A human embryonic stage in which about 100 cells are
arranged around a central cavity.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>blastocyst</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>141) Identify the following terms related to the nervous
system from their definitions for 1 and 4/11 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>The functional unit of the nervous system,</span>
specialized for transmitting signals from one location in the body to another.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>neurons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Neuron extensions, or processes, which convey signals from
their tips to the rest of the neuron.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>dendrites</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Neuron extensions, or processes, which conduct messages
toward the tips of the neuron.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>axons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The muscle or gland cells that <span class=GramE>actually
carry</span> out the body's responses to stimuli.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>effector cells</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Ropelike bundles of extensions of neurons tightly wrapped in
connective tissue.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nerves</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A layer of insulating cells enclosing axons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>myelin sheath</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Specialized endings of axon branches which relay signals to
other cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>synaptic terminals<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The site of contact between a synaptic terminal and a target
cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>synapse</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Neurons that communicate information about the external and
internal environments from sensory receptors to the central nervous system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sensory neurons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Neurons that convey impulses from the central nervous system
to effector cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>motor neurons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Neurons that integrate sensory input and motor output, making
connections only with other neurons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>interneurons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A simple, automated response resulting from a neuron circuit
of sensory and motor neurons, without signals passing to the brain.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>reflex</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A cluster of nerve cell bodies in the peripheral nervous
system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ganglion</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Functional clusters of nerves in the brain.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nuclei</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Supporting cells that provide the structure for the nervous
system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glia</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the two cations and the anion most important in the
generation of neural signals.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sodium, potassium</u>; <u>chloride</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cell transmitting a signal.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>presynaptic cell</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The cell receiving a signal.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>postsynaptic cell</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A system of nerves that branch throughout the body, present
in some cnidarians.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nerve net</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A thick bundle of nerves usually extending longitudinally
through the body from the brain.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nerve cord</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>142) Identify the following terms related to the brain from
their definitions for 1.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The stalk and caplike swellings at the anterior end of the
spinal cord.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>brainstem</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The portion of the brainstem that controls several visceral
functions, including breathing, heart and blood vessel activity, swallowing,
vomiting, and digestion.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>medulla oblongata</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The portion of the brainstem that performs some of the same
functions as the medulla and helps control movement.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pons</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The portion of the brainstem that coordinates sensory
information.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>midbrain</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The nucleus in the midbrain that controls auditory
information.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>inferior colliculum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The nucleus in the midbrain that controls visual
information.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>superior colliculum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The part of the brain that functions in unconscious coordination
of movement and balance.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cerebellum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The part of the brain that includes a projection called the
pineal gland and a choroid plexus, which is one of several clusters of
capillaries that produce cerebrospinal fluid.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>epithalamus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The part of the brain that serves as an input center for
sensory information going to the cerebrum and an output center for motor
information leaving the cerebrum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thalamus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The small part of the brain that controls homeostatic <span
class=GramE>regulation, and</span> contains the body's thermostat and centers
for regulating hunger, thirst, and other survival mechanisms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hypothalamus</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The combination of the epithalamus, thalamus, and
hypothalamus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>diencephalon<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>The dorsal portion of the forebrain,</span>
divided into left and right hemispheres, that is the integrating center for
memory, learning, emotions, and other complex functions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cerebrum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Centers for motor coordination in the cerebrum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>basal nuclei</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The surface of the cerebrum, containing sensory and motor
nerve cell bodies, that is the largest and most complex part of the brain.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cerebral cortex</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The thick band of fibers that connects the right and left
portions of the cerebral cortex.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>corpus callosum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A test that monitors brain electrical activity.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>electroencephalogram (EEG)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the four main lobes of the cerebrum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>frontal, parietal, occipital, temporal</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>143) Identify the following types of receptors from their
descriptions for 2 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Pain receptors in the skin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nociceptors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Receptors that signal surface and body core temperature.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thermoreceptors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Receptors that transmit information about solute
concentrations and that respond to individual kinds of molecules.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chemoreceptors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Taste receptors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>gustatory receptors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Smell receptors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>olfactory receptors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Receptors that detect electromagnetic energy.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>electromagnetic receptors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Receptors that detect visible light.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>photoreceptors</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>144) Identify the following terms related to the eye from
their definitions for two points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The tough, white outer layer of connective tissue along the
globe of the eyeball.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sclera</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The thin, pigmented inner layer of the eyeball.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>choroid</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A mucous membrane formed by a delicate layer of epithelial
cells that covers the outer surface of the sclera and helps keep the eye moist.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>conjunctiva</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The transparent portion of the sclera that lets light into
the eye and acts as a fixed lens.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cornea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The anterior portion of the choroid that gives the eye its
color.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>iris</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The hole in the center of the iris through which light
enters.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pupil</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The innermost layer of the eyeball, containing the
photoreceptor cells.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>retina</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The clear, watery substance that fills the anterior cavity
of the eye.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aqueous humor</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The component of the eye that produces the aqueous humor.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ciliary body</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A disease caused by blockage of the ducts that drain the
aqueous humor, causing pressure build-up that compresses the retina.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>glaucoma</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The jellylike substance in the posterior cavity that
constitutes most of the volume of the eye.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>vitreous humor</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of photoreceptor cells that are <span class=GramE>very
sensitive</span> to light but not to color.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>rods</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of photoreceptor cells that can distinguish colors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cones</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The visual pigment consisting of retinal and opsin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>rhodopsin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The place near the center of the base of the cerebral cortex
where the optic nerves from the two eyes meet.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>optic chiasm</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>145) Answer the following related to the ear for 1 and 7/8
points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three major regions of the ear.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>outer ear, middle ear, inner ear</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the structure separating the outer ear from the middle
ear, also known as the eardrum.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tympanic membrane</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three small bones in the middle ear.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>malleus (hammer), incus (anvil), stapes (stirrup)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the tube that connects the middle ear to the pharynx,
allowing the middle ear to equalize pressure with the atmosphere.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Eustachian tube</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the complex, coiled organ in the inner ear involved in
hearing.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cochlea</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the organ at the floor of the cochlear duct that
contains the actual receptor cells of the ear.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>organ of Corti</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three structures in the inner ear, two of them in
the vestibule, that help maintain balance.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>utricle, saccule, semicircular canals</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the mechanoreceptor system consisting of a series of
pores and receptor units along the sides of the body, that detects water
movements made by an animal itself and by other moving objects.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lateral line system</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the receptor units of the lateral line system.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>neromasts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the sensory organs that contain mechanoreceptors and
function in their sense of equilibrium.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>statocysts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>146) Identify the following terms related to the skeletal
system from their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of skeleton consisting of fluid held under pressure
in a closed body compartment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>hydrostatic skeleton</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A hard encasement deposited on the surface of an animal.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>exoskeleton</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A system of hard supporting elements, such as bones, buried
within the soft tissues of an animal.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>endoskeleton</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the three major types of bone joints.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ball-and-socket, hinge, pivot</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>Jaw bone</span></p>
