<p class=MsoNormal>148) Identify the following terms related to the muscles
from their definitions for three points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Name the two filaments that slide past each other, causing
muscle contraction.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>actin, myosin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Filaments consisting of strands of actin or myosin.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>myofilaments</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>A bundle of myofilaments,</span> arranged
longitudinally.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>myofibrils</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The repeating, basic functional unit of muscles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sarcomere</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A specialized endoplasmic reticulum that regulates calcium
concentration in the muscle cell.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>sarcoplasmic reticulum<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of muscle fiber used for rapid, powerful
contractions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fast muscle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of muscle fiber that can sustain long contractions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>slow muscle<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The type of muscle in the heart.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cardiac muscle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of muscle fiber whose actin and myosin filaments are
not regularly arrayed, and which cannot generate much tension but can contract
over a large range of lengths.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>smooth muscle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>149) Identify the following terms related to ecology from
their definitions for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An individual living creature.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>organism</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A group of individuals of the same species living in a <span
class=GramE>particular geographic</span> area.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>population</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>All the organisms that inhabit a particular <span
class=GramE>area;</span> an assemblage of populations of different species.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>community</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>All the organisms in a given area, as well as the abiotic
factors with which they <span class=GramE>interact;</span> a community and its
physical environment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ecosystem</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The global ecosystem; the sum of all the plant's ecosystems.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>biosphere</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The general term for a major type of ecosystem that occupies
broad geographic regions and is characterized by its climate.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>biome</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The warming of Earth due to the atmospheric accumulation of
carbon dioxide, which absorbs infrared radiation and slows its escape from the
irradiated Earth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>greenhouse</u> effect</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>150) Identify the following terms related to aquatic biomes
from their definitions for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The upper zone of an aquatic biome in which there is
sufficient light for photosynthesis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>photic zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The lower zone of an aquatic biome where little light
penetrates.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aphotic zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A narrow stratum of rapid temperature change that separates
a more uniformly warm upper layer from a more uniformly cold deeper layer.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>thermocline</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The substrate made of sand and sediments at the bottom of
all aquatic biomes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>benthic zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The community of organisms inhabiting the benthic zone.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>benthos</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An area covered with water that supports aquatic plants.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>wetland</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The area where a freshwater stream or river merges with the
ocean, often bordered by coastal wetlands called mudflats and saltmarshes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>estuary</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>151) Identify the following terms related to freshwater
biomes from their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The shallow, well-lit waters close to shore in a freshwater
biome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>littoral zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The well-lit, open surface waters further from shore in a
freshwater biome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>limnetic zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The deep, aphotic region of a freshwater biome.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>profundal zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Deep, nutrient-poor lakes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oligotrophic</u> lakes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Shallow, high-nutrient lakes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>eutrophic</u> lakes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Lakes with a moderate amount of nutrients and phytoplankton
productivity.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mesotrophic</u> lakes</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>152) Identify the following terms related to marine biomes
from their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The zone where land meets water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>intertidal zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The shallow regions over continental shelves.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>neritic zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The deep regions past the continental shelves.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oceanic zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Open water of any depth.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pelagic zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A biome common in warm tropical neritic zones dominated by
large structures of cnidarians.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coral reefs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Deep, cold, dark, high-pressure, low-nutrient, benthic
zones.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>abyssal zone</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>153) Identify the following terrestrial biomes from their
descriptions for 3.75 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have pronounced vertical stratification, dense
vegetation, and <span class=GramE>usually high</span> rainfall. Trees in the
canopy make up the topmost stratum, which is often closed, allowing little
light to reach the ground below.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tropical forests</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have a rainy season and a dry season and are dominated
by grasses, small broadleaf plants called forbs, large herbivores, and
predators.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>savannas</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have less than thirty centimeters of rainfall per <span
class=GramE>year, but</span> may be either hot or cold.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>deserts</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have mild, rainy winters and long, hot, dry summers,
and are dominated by dense, spiny, evergreen shrubs.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>chaparrals</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have fertile soil and seasonal <span class=GramE>droughts,
and</span> are often used for farmland. Examples include the veldts of South
Africa, the puszta of Hungary, the pampas of Argentina, the steppes of Russia,
and the plains and prairies of central North America.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
temperate <u>grasslands</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They are common in the midlatitudes and are dominated by
dense strands of trees that lose their leaves before winter.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
temperate <u>deciduous forests<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have a warm, moist climate and are dominated by
cone-bearing trees.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>coniferous forests<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>They have bitterly cold temperatures and high winds and
receive little rainfall. Water cannot penetrate the underlying <span
class=GramE>perpetually-frozen</span> permafrost, so water and snow accumulate
on the shallow topsoil.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>tundras</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>154) Identify the following terms related to behavioral
biology from their definitions for 2.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The research field that studies how animals behave in their
natural habitats.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ethology</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A sequence of behavioral acts that is essentially
unchangeable and usually carried to completion once initiated.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fixed action pattern (FAP)</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of learning that is limited to a specific <span
class=GramE>time period</span> in an animal's life and that is generally
irreversible.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>imprinting</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The ability of an animal's nervous system to perceive,
store, process, and use information gathered by sensory receptors.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cognition</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A simple change in activity rate in response to a stimulus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>kinesis</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A <span class=GramE>more or less automatic</span>, oriented
movement toward or away from some stimulus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>taxis<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Regular movement of a species over relatively long
distances.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>migration</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of contest involving both threatening and submissive
behavior that determines which competitor gains access to some resource.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>agonistic</u> behavior</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The use of symbolic activity in agonistic behavior.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ritual</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Social groups dominated by agonistic behavior, in which
there is a clear &quot;pecking order.&quot;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>dominance hierarchy</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>An area that an individual defends, usually excluding other
members of its own species.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>territory</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A small area in which bird or insect males display
communally.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>lek</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>155) Identify the following terms related to population
ecology from their definitions for 3 and 1/3 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The number of individuals per unit of area or volume.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>density</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The pattern of spacing among individuals within the geographical
boundaries of the population.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>dispersion</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The most common pattern of dispersion, in which individuals
are aggregated in patches.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>clumped</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The spatial variation, or environmental patchiness, of
individual organisms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>grain</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The study of the vital statistics that affect population
size.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>demography</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A group of individuals of the same age.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cohort</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A life history pattern in which most energy is expended in a
single large reproductive effort.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>semelparity</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A life history pattern in which a few offspring are produced
at a time over a span of many seasons.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>iteroparity</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The maximum population size that a <span class=GramE>particular
environment</span> can support with no net increase or decrease over a
relatively long period of time.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>carrying capacity</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>156) Identify the following terms related to animal defenses
against predators from their definitions for five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of passive defense, also known as camouflage, that
makes potential prey difficult to spot against its background.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>cryptic coloration</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of defense in which an animal has <span class=GramE>brightly-colored</span>
features to warn predators that it has effective chemical defenses.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>aposematic coloration</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of defense in which an animal bears a superficial
resemblance to another species.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>mimicry</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The species which the mimic resembles.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>model</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of mimicry in which a palatable or harmless species
mimics an unpalatable or harmful model.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Batesian mimicry</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of mimicry in which two or more unpalatable,
aposematically colored species resemble each other.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>Mullerian mimicry</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>157) Identify the following terms related to community
ecology from their definitions for 4 and 2/7 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The <span class=GramE>sum total</span> of an organism's use
of the biotic and abiotic resources in its environment.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ecological niche</u> (prompt on just niche)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The set of resources a population is theoretically capable
of using under ideal circumstances.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>fundamental niche</u> (prompt on just niche)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The resources a population <span class=GramE>actually uses</span>.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>realized niche</u> (prompt on just niche)</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The environment in which an organism lives.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>habitat</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Transition in the species composition of a biological
community.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>ecological succession</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of ecological succession that begins with a virtually
lifeless area where soil has not yet formed.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primary succession</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A type of ecological succession that begins where an
existing community has been cleared by some disturbance that leaves the soil
intact.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>secondary succession<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>158) Identify the following terms related to ecosystems from
their definitions for 2 and 4/13 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The different feeding relationships in an ecosystem that
determine the route of energy flow and the pattern of chemical cycling.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>trophic structure<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The division of species in an ecosystem <span class=GramE>on
the basis of</span> their main nutritional source.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>trophic level</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The trophic level, consisting of autotrophs, that ultimately
supports all others in an ecosystem.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primary producers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The trophic level consisting of herbivores that eat plants
or algae.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>primary consumers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The trophic level consisting of carnivores that eat
herbivores.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>secondary consumers</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The pathway along which food is transferred from trophic
level to trophic level.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>food chain</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The complex, interwoven feeding relationships in an
ecosystem.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>food webs</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The rate of incorporation of energy and materials into the
bodies of organisms.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>production</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The metabolic use of assimilated organic materials for
growth and reproduction.<span style='mso-tab-count:1'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>consumption</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The breakdown of organic materials to inorganic ones.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>decomposition</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Total primary productivity minus the energy used by the
producers for respiration.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>net primary productivity</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span class=GramE>Primary productivity,</span> expressed in
terms of energy per unit area per unit time.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>biomass</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>A diagram representing ecological productivity in which the
trophic levels are stacked in blocks with primary producers forming the
foundation.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>pyramid</u> of productivity</p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>159) Identify the following biochemical cycles from their
descriptions for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>On a global scale, evaporation exceeds precipitation over
the oceans. The result is a net movement of water vapor, carried by winds, from
the ocean to the land. The excess of precipitation over evaporation on land
results in the formation of surface and groundwater systems that flow back to
the sea, completing the major part of the cycle. On land, more than ninety
percent of the vaporization is due to plant transpiration, which together with
other types of evaporation is referred to as evapotranspiration.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>water cycle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>The reciprocal processes of photosynthesis and cellular
respiration are responsible for the major transformations and movements of this
element. A seasonal pulse in atmospheric carbon dioxide is caused by decreased
photosynthetic activity during the Northern Hemisphere's winter. On a global
scale, the return of carbon dioxide to the atmosphere by respiration closely
balances its removal by photosynthesis. However, the burning of wood and fossil
fuels adds more carbon dioxide to the atmosphere.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>carbon cycle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>Most of this element cycling through food webs is taken up
by plants in the form of nitrate. Most of this, in turn, comes from the
nitrification of ammonium that results from the decomposition of organic
material. The addition of this element from the atmosphere and its return via
denitrification involve relatively small amounts compared to the local
recycling that occurs in the soil or water. </p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>nitrogen cycle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This element, which does not have an atmospheric component,
tends to cycle locally. Generally, small losses from terrestrial systems caused
by leaching are balanced by gains from the weathering of rocks. Often the
element is cycled through food webs. Some is lost from the ecosystem because of
chemical precipitation or through settling of detritus to the bottom.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>phosphorous cycle</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>160) Identify the following people important in the
development of organic chemistry for 7.5 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This Swedish chemist was the first to make the distinction
between organic compounds and inorganic compounds.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Jons Jakob <u>Berzelius</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This German chemist accidentally synthesized the organic
compound urea from ammonium and cyanate ions.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Friedrich <u>Wohler</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This student of Friedrich Wohler made the organic compound
acetic acid from inorganic substances that could themselves be prepared
directly from pure elements.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Hermann <u>Kolbe</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>While a graduate student at the University of Chicago, this
American used a laboratory simulation of chemical conditions on the primitive
Earth to demonstrate that the spontaneous synthesis of organic compounds could
have been an early stage in the origin of life.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Stanley <u>Miller</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>161) Identify the following people important in the study of
cell membranes for 3.75 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1895, this scientist postulated that membranes are made
of lipids, based on his observations that substances that dissolve in lipids
enter cells much more rapidly than substances that are insoluble in lipids.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Charles <u>Overton</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1917, this scientist made artificial membranes by adding
phospholipids dissolved in benzene to water.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Irving <u>Langmuir</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1925, these two Dutch scientists reasoned that cell
membranes must <span class=GramE>actually be</span> phospholipid bilayers.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
E. <u>Gorter</u> and F. <u>Grendel</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1935, these two scientists proposed a sandwich model of
membranes, suggesting a phospholipid bilayer between two layers of globular
protein.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Hugh <u>Davson</u> and James <u>Danielli</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1972, these two scientists advocated the fluid mosaic
model of membranes, suggesting that proteins are dispersed and individually
inserted into the phospholipid bilayer.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
S.J. <u>Singer</u> and G. <u>Nicolson</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>162) Identify the following people important in the study of
DNA for 2 and 8/11 points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1928, this British medical officer conducted experiments
injecting mice with pneumonia-causing <span class=GramE>bacteria, and</span>
reached the conclusion that molecules from dead pathogenic bacteria could
genetically transform living non-pathogenic bacteria into pathogenic bacteria.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Frederick <u>Griffith</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This American bacteriologist purified various chemicals from
Griffith's heat-killed pathogenic bacteria, attempting to determine the
identity of the transforming substance, and finally concluded that it was DNA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Oswald <u>Avery</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1952, these two scientists demonstrated that DNA, not
protein, functions as the genetic material in the T2 phage by labeling viral
proteins with radioactive sulfur and viral DNA with radioactive phosphorus.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Alfred <u>Hersey</u> and Martha <u>Chase</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This biochemist discovered that the number of adenines
approximately equaled the number of thymines, and the number of guanines
approximately equaled the number of cytosines, in the DNA of all species he
studied.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Erwin <u>Chargaff</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These two scientists proposed the double-helix structure of
DNA.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
James <u>Watson</u> and Francis <u>Crick</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This Englishwoman was the X-ray crystallographer who took
the photo that enabled Watson and Crick to deduce the double-helical structure
of DNA&gt;</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Rosalind <u>Franklin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This colleague of Rosalind Franklin at King's College in
London shared the 1962 Nobel Prize with Watson and Crick.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Maurice <u>Wilkins</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These two scientists confirmed the semiconservative
hypothesis of DNA replication by culturing E. coli on a medium containing a
heavy isotope of nitrogen and observing the proportion of new nitrogen in each
generation of replicated DNA strands.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Matthew <u>Meselson</u> and Franklin <u>Stahl</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>163) Identify the following people important in the study of
proteins for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1909, this British physician first suggested that genes
dictate phenotypes through enzymes that catalyze specific chemical processes in
the cell, and that the symptoms of an inherited disease reflect a person's
inability to make a <span class=GramE>particular enzyme</span>.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Archibald <u>Garrod</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>These two scientists developed the one gene - one enzyme
hypothesis based on their experiments growing different types of mutant red
bread molds that could not produce the amino acid arginine on nutritional
mediums with different intermediates in arginine synthesis.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
George <u>Beadle</u> and Edward <u>Tatum</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In 1961, this scientist was the first to decipher a codon in
the genetic code, determining that a &quot;poly-U&quot; string translated into
a polypeptide with only the amino acid phenylalanine.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Marshall <u>Nirenberg</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>In the 1920s, this scientist recognized the mutagenic
potential of high-energy radiation when he discovered that if he subjected
fruit flies to X-rays, genetic changes increased in frequency.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Hermann <u>Muller</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>164) Identify the following people important in the study of
evolution for six points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This French anatomist advocated catastrophism, speculating
that each boundary between strata in the fossil record corresponded in time to
a catastrophe that had destroyed many of the species living there at that time.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Georges <u>Cuvier</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This Scottish geologist advocated gradualism, which holds
that profound change is the cumulative product of slow but continuous
processes.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
James <u>Hutton</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This Scottish geologist advocated uniformitarianism, which
holds that geological processes have not changed throughout Earth's history. He
also published <i>Principles of Geology</i>.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Charles <u>Lyell</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This French scientist published a comprehensive theory of
evolution in 1809, including a mechanism to explain how specific adaptations
evolve, incorporating the ideas of use and disuse and the inheritance of
acquired characteristics.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Jean Baptiste <u>Lamarck</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>This English scientist sailed on the <i>Beagle</i>, proposed
descent with modification and natural selection, and published <i>The Origin of
Species</i> in 1859.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
Charles <u>Darwin</u></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></p>

<p class=MsoNormal>165) Name, in decreasing order of the percent of human body
weight they constitute, the six most common elements in the human body, for
five points each.</p>

<p class=MsoNormal>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Answer:
<u>oxygen (65.0%), carbon (18.5%), hydrogen (9.5%), nitrogen (3.3%), calcium
